Diane Papan 
Amourence Lee 
CITY OF SAN MATEO 
Special Meeting Minutes 
City Council 
City Hall 
330 W. 20th Avenue 
San Mateo CA 94403 
www.cityofsanmateo.org 
  
Monday, October 19, 2020 
Remote 5:30 PM 
Special Meeting 
 
  
CALL TO ORDER This meeting is being held under the provisions of State of California Governor Gavin Newsom’s 
Executive Order N-29-20; in which Brown Act regulations are relaxed to allow members to remote in due to the 
Coronavirus Covid-19 health emergency. 
Roll Call 
  
Remote:    Mayor Goethals, Deputy Mayor Rodriguez, Council Members: Bonilla, Papan and Lee 
 
STUDY SESSION  
1. 
Fiscal Sustainability Plan – Update 
Finance Director Rich Lee provided an overview and update on the City’s Fiscal Sustainability Plan Phase 1. Council 
asked questions of staff. Lee noted the City is better prepared than we were in the great recession to absorb the 
volatility in an economic downturn. Public Comment – there were no speakers. Council was appreciative of the 
report and information provided.  
2. 
Short-Term Rental Regulation Policy Options 
Management Analyst Denise Garcia provided a presentation on short-term rental regulations policy options for 
the Council to consider. Council asked questions of staff. Staff sought direction on the following policy 
recommendations: 1) prohibit special events; 2) limit the number of occupants; 3) restrict parking to on-site; 4) 
require local contact person; and 5) limit the number of rental days per calendar year. 
Public Comment – Mark Grieco, President Baywood Homeowners Association, spoke of impacts in their 
neighborhood and expressed interest in hosted versus non-hosted. Lisa Diaz Nash stated this is a good start and 
outlined several additional recommendations. Rob Dougherty inquired about considering limiting the number of 
short-term rentals and if there is research if having short-term rentals impacts neighboring property values. Roger 
Oser, Baywood Homeowners Association, the biggest issue is the number of allowed occupants which should be 
limited to two per bedroom.  
Council discussion ensued and Council directed staff to bring back policies that include provisions to prohibit 
special events; limit the number of occupants to up to two per bedroom and up to a total house maximum of 10; 
require a local contact person with 24/7 access; require on-site parking for short term rental guests; limit un-
hosted rental days to 120 per year; develop complaint procedures; investigate potentially not charging permit 
fees for hosted units; and staff to explore additional details of what a contact tree for 24/7 contact could be.  
 
ADJOURNMENT - The meeting adjourned at 6:59 p.m. 
 
APPROVED BY:                                                          
SUBMITTED BY: 
 
 
                                                                                        
                                                            
Joe Goethals, Mayor                                                    
Patrice M. Olds, City Clerk

MEETING DATE:
November 2, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Classification Updates – City Clerk's Department
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the updates to the Fair Labor Standards Act status and Bargaining Unit representation of 
the Deputy City Clerk classification and revisions to the job specification for the classification of Deputy City Clerk. 
BACKGROUND:
A review of the Deputy City Clerk classification was conducted to evaluate if it should be exempt from overtime provisions 
of the Fair Labor Standards Act (FLSA) and if it is more correctly suited for representation in the Management Unit. This 
involved an exemption test and a review of the criteria for classification in the Management Unit. After completion of this 
analysis, it was determined that the position qualified as FLSA exempt and that based on the core responsibilities, 
independent judgement, and supervisory role, the position would be more accurately represented by the Management 
Unit. 
Consequently, the Human Resources Department recommends updating the Deputy City Clerk classification to indicate it is 
FLSA exempt and represented by the Management Unit. The proposed new job specification reflects these changes and 
includes updates made to the Deputy City Clerk job specification in 2017 by the Specialized Support focus group as part of 
the core competency project to more accurately reflect the duties performed by the employee in this position. The San 
Mateo City Employees’ Association that currently represents this classification and the San Mateo Management 
Employees’ Association proposed to represent this classification were notified of this change and have no objections to it. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact from this classification update.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This classification update is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will 
not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS 
Att 1 – Proposed Resolution 
             Exhibit 1 – Job Specification 
Att 2 – Job Specification with tracked changes

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. __ (2020)
CLASSIFICATION UPDATES IN CITY CLERK’S DEPARTMENT
WHEREAS, pursuant to the San Mateo Municipal Code Section 2.57.030(d), approval of classifications and 
related job specifications and salary schedules, reclassification of employees, modifications to job specifications 
and abolishment of an existing classification must be approved by City Council Resolution; and
WHEREAS, the proposed classification updates are as detailed below:

Update the Deputy City Clerk classification as Fair Labor Standards Act (FLSA) exempt and represented 
by the Management Unit, and;

Revise the job specification for the classification of Deputy City Clerk.
WHEREAS, the employee associations representing the classification have reviewed the proposed changes 
and have not brought forth any objections or concerns; 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, RESOLVES that the 
following classification updates is approved:
1.
The updates to the Deputy City Clerk position as FLSA exempt and represented by the Management 
Unit, and;
2.
The revisions to the job specification for the classification of Deputy City Clerk attached as Exhibit 1.
11 of 312

--- page 12 ---
EXHIBIT 1
DEPUTY CITY CLERK
DEFINITION
Using independent judgement, plan, organize, direct and perform a variety of complex administrative, 
technical, and supervisory duties in support of the City Clerk Department’s day-to-day operations, 
primarily legislative operations and contract and process management; provide a high level of 
administrative and technical support to the City Clerk and other departments and perform all duties of the 
City Clerk in his/her absence.
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED
Receives general supervision from the City Clerk.
Exercises functional and technical supervision over administrative staff.
DISTINGUISHING CHARACTERISTICS
This is a single position class responsible for assisting the City Clerk in administration of the City Clerk 
Department’s operations. The incumbent works under the direction of the City Clerk and exercises 
supervision over administrative, intern and volunteer positions.
EXAMPLES OF DUTIES
Duties may include, but are not limited to, the following:
Assist the City Clerk in performing the day-to-day functions of the City Clerk's office; and in the absence 
of the City Clerk, act as City Clerk, performing such duties as attending meetings, writing agenda reports, 
taking minutes, certifying ordinances, resolutions, agreements and other official documents, administer 
oaths of office and supervise staff.
Implement and manage the agenda production process including maintaining a deep knowledge of the 
agenda management software and process; training staff in the use of the software and process; and assist 
in deploying consistent agenda practices across the organization; coordinating with other departments on 
agenda content; enforcing work product standards and holding departments and higher classifications 
responsible for meeting standards and deadlines; and producing the agenda and agenda packet per state 
law and city requirements.
Manage the publication of legal and public notices, for all Council bodies, in accordance with City, State 
and Federal law, and filing, indexing, certifying, processing for recordation, and safeguarding of all City 
Council proceedings. 
Attend City Council meetings with the City Clerk to assist with operating the audio / visual / agenda / 
voting system and take minutes as required.
12 of 312

--- page 13 ---
Responsible for after Council action including producing and maintaining official City records and 
documents in good order such as resolutions, ordinances, contracts, deeds, correspondence, inter-agency

DEPUTY CITY CLERK 
DEFINITION 
 
Using independent judgement, plan, organize, direct and perform a variety of complex administrative, 
technical, and supervisory duties in support of the City Clerk Department’s day-to-day operations, 
primarily legislative operations and contract and process management; provide a high level of 
administrative and technical support to the City Clerk and other departments and perform all duties of the 
City Clerk in his/her absence. 
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED 
 
Receives general supervision from the City Clerk. 
 
Exercises functional and technical supervision over administrative staff. 
 
DISTINGUISHING CHARACTERISTICS 
 
This is a single position class responsible for assisting the City Clerk in administration of the City Clerk 
Department’s operations. The incumbent works under the direction of the City Clerk and exercises 
supervision over administrative, intern and volunteer positions. 
 
EXAMPLES OF DUTIES 
Duties may include, but are not limited to, the following: 
 
Assist the City Clerk in performing the day-to-day functions of the City Clerk's office; and in the absence 
of the City Clerk, act as City Clerk, performing such duties as attending meetings, writing agenda reports, 
taking minutes, certifying ordinances, resolutions, agreements and other official documents, administer 
oaths of office and supervise staff. 
 
Implement and manage the agenda production process including maintaining a deep knowledge of the 
agenda management software and process; training staff in the use of the software and process; and assist 
in deploying consistent agenda practices across the organization; coordinating with other departments on 
agenda content; enforcing work product standards and holding departments and higher classifications 
responsible for meeting standards and deadlines; and producing the agenda and agenda packet per state 
law and city requirements. 
 
Manage the publication of legal and public notices, for all Council bodies, in accordance with City, State 
and Federal law, and filing, indexing, certifying, processing for recordation, and safeguarding of all City 
Council proceedings.  
 
Attend City Council meetings with the City Clerk to assist with operating the audio / visual / agenda / 
voting system and take minutes as required.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  4
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
File ID: 20-3744
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Finance Department
MEETING DATE:
November 02, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Parking Citation Processing – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with Turbo Data Systems, Inc. for the purpose of parking citation processing 
and adjudication services to extend the term expiration to June 30, 2021.
BACKGROUND:
The City of San Mateo entered into an agreement with Turbo Data Systems, Inc. (Turbo Data) to provide parking citations 
processing and adjudication services for a five-year period beginning July 2015 and ending in June 2020. Turbo Data was 
selected as part of a comprehensive effort led by the County of San Mateo in collaboration with the San Mateo Finance 
Officers Group (SAMFOG). In anticipation of the agreement expiration, a working group led by the County of San Mateo's 
County Manager's Office began to work on issuing a Request for Proposals (RFP). The group also included the finance 
directors from the City of Daly City, Belmont, and San Mateo to represent the interests of the local municipalities. The 
group's efforts had culminated in a rough draft of the RFP being circulated for review, with plans to publish the RFP and 
award agreement by the end of May 2020. Unfortunately, the RFP process was postponed due to COVID-19 and the 
shelter-in-place health order. The group plans on reconvening in the near term to begin the RFP process again. As such, 
the only amendment to the agreement is extension of the term to June 30, 2021. All other agreement provisions remain 
the same. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
This agreement amendment will have no impact on the cost of the parking citation processing and adjudication services. 
No supplemental budget appropriations are required.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that 
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Amendment
Att 2 – Turbo Data Agreement

through June 30, 2020.

Contractor's duty to indemnify and save harmless under this Section shall not apply to injuries or

by reason of its own negligence or willful misconduct.

issue; and/or (b) any aspects of the services under this Agreement which have been used by City in a

the parties.

regard to its choice of law or conflict of law rules. Any dispute arising out of this Agreement shall be
venued either in the San Mateo County Superior Court or in the United States District Court for the
Northern District of California.

Exhibit A
In consideration of the payments set forth in Exhibit B, Contractor shall provide the following services:

Parking Citation Processing

A. Basic Processing — Contractor will enter manual citations and citation dispositions into Customer's
database within 2 business days. The basic service includes database maintenance, daily system
backups, toll-free phone number for the public, Interactive Voice Response System (/VRS) with
customized recorded information and citation lookup capability, pticket.com web-based Inquiry
System for the public with customized content, Contractor's Customer Service Representatives
(9:00 am — 5:00 pm, Monday through Friday, excluding holidays) to speak with the public regarding
parking citation issues, ongoing Client support, and documentation and training for use of the
Contractor-provided online system. Contractor will process correction notices and notify each
Customer of citations unable to be entered for any reason, (such as no violation code, unreadable
license, etc.).

B. Hand held Ticket writer Interface - Contractor will provide for automated import of electronic
citations into Customer's database. Batch files will be uploaded immediately upon file transfer.
Contractor will maintain and update the hot sheet or scofflaw files on a daily basis for Customer,
identifying vehicles which have accumulated five (5) or more outstanding citations in the combined
San Mateo County contract area to upload into their handheld ticket writers. Contractor will provide
electronic reports on a monthly basis. Contractor will work with Customer to implement any changes
required for handheld ticket writer equipment.

C. Customer Service and Toll-Free Telephone Number — Contractor will provide a toll-free automated
telephone number for inquiries and credit card payments. The toll-free telephone service will be
available a minimum of 20 hours per day, 7 days per week for the 50 United States and Canada, with
the exception of backup time sometime between the hours of midnight and 4:00 am. A customized
recorded voice response system in English and Spanish will be available to provide information for
each payor on how fo pay and contest citations, registration violation information, and Customer
address information. The automated telephone system will be capable of receiving a minimum of
20,000 incoming calls per month. Downtime for required maintenance will be between midnight and
4:00 a.m. The automated voice response system will be capable of providing real-time data regarding
the citation issue date, amount due, delinquent date and total amount due for each license plate when
multiple citations are outstanding. The system will provide information about appealed citations and
the results of the appeal, Contractor Customer Service Representatives (CSRs) will be available
Monday through Friday, 9:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., excluding Customer recognized holidays. CSRs will be
available to provide instructions and information on general parking policies and procedures, and
administrative adjudication procedures for the Customer. At least one CSR will be available for
Spanish translation during regular business hours Monday through Friday. Calls will be answered in
six rings or less. In order to assist CSRs with non-English speakers, AT&T’s Language Line will be
available at all times the CSRs are available and shall be employed to accomplish translations as
required. The telephone system will provide up-to-date information on the status of a citation with the
option to speak with a five representative during normal business hours. CSR's will provide customer
service for the public in resolving parking citation questions of a non-judicial nature and research
specific citation data when necessary. CSRs will be fully trained in all informational aspects of parking
citation processing and related information specific to the Customer.

D. System and Document Storage ~ Contractor will retain all citations paid or dismissed on the
computer system for 3 years and then removed. Unpaid citations will be retained on the computer

Page 8

S&nbsp;
33 of&nbsp;312


--- page 34 ---
system for 5 years and then removed. Citation documents will be stored for 2 years from date of issue
and then returned to Customer or shredded. Payment documents will be stored for 2 years from the
date of payment and then returned to Customer or shredded.

. Online Reporting — Contractor will provide regular daily, weekly and monthly reports in a format as
agreed upon. Additional reports will be provided at no additional cost for operating, production and
audit functions. Reports will be made available online via a secure web page and be available for
Customer access no later than the thirtieth (30th) day of the following month, except when February is
the following month, in which case this information will be available by the last day of February.

DMV Interface for Registered Owner Name Retrieval — Contractor will obtain names and addresses
of registered owners of cited vehicles from California DMV using online or manual access to registered
owner information from California DMV when necessary. Upon return of registered owner information
from DMV, Contractor will validate vehicle make. Contractor will also review DMV “No Hit’ list to
ensure that license plate and state have been entered correctly.

. Notice Processing ~ Contractor will print the required Notice and mail to each registered owner
whose name has been retrieved within 10 to 21 days after the citation has been issued. This includes
second notices mailed for bounced checks, partial payments, and name or address changes.
Contractor is required to send notices to lessees or renters of cited vehicles when provided with
proof of a written lease or rental agreement. All postage, notice forms and envelopes will be provided
by Contractor. All notices and letters will be formatted using custom #10 window envelopes with the
Customer's return address. The interior #9 return envelope will be customized with the Customers
payment address. Drive Away Notices will be mailed by first class mail to registered owners of vehicles
that drive away from the officer at citation issuance time as required by the California Vehicle Code.
Notices are mailed no later than 15 days from the date of the original citation to the registered owner of
the vehicle. Delinquent Notices generated will be mailed at least once a week by first class mail to
registered owners. Returned check notices will be mailed by first class mail to individuals immediately
upon notification from the Customer that a check has been retumed for non-payment. These notices
will state the amount of original penalty, delinquent amount, and the appropriate returned check fee.
Partial Payment Notices will be sent by first class mail to those who do not pay the full penalty amount.
The notice will indicate the amount that was paid and the remainder that is due. The Contractor will
generate Reminder Notices for unpaid accounts at a time frame acceptable to the Customer.
Contractor will communicate with violators in a timely manner by mail in response to correspondence
such as incomplete registration, citation, or payment information.

. Additional Notices- Contractor will mail Other Correspondence as required for processing.
Adjudication Letters will be mailed as required. DMV Hold Letters shall be mailed to registered owners
on citations remaining open 18 months after a DMV Hold is placed.

DMV Interface for Placing Registration Holds — Contractor will transmit a Notice of Delinquency to
the California DMV for vehicles with California license plates after a Notice of Violation has been
mailed to the registered owner and Contractor has not received notification that the citation has
been cleared. This Notice of Delinquency will be transmitted to the California DMV within 2
business days after the date specified by the Customer to be the DMV Date.

DMV Interface for Releasing Registration Holds - Contractor will transmit a Notice to the

California DMV that a Notice of Delinquency has been cleared within 2 business days after Contractor
has received notification of clearance.

N. Out of State Citations - Contractor will process citations for non-California license plates by entering
the citation information into the system database and report them along with all other citations on the
database with the standard reports. If they become delinquent, requests for registered owner
information will be sent to the appropriate out-of-state DMV. The Notice of Intent will be generated to
the registered owner and the fine amount requested. Contractor will incur all costs for out of state
name retrieval, including out-of-state DMV fees and charges. Contractor will receive payment from
Customer based on the amount of revenues collected from out-of-state citations after the Notice of
Intent has been issued.

Q. Public On-Line Access — www.pticket.com - Contractor will supply a web site for public use
allowing the receiver of a parking violation to enter the parking citation number or other identifying
information in order to view parking citation data on line in real time. The website incorporates the
highest level of data security and data privacy in the industry. Web-based data traffic, which includes
names, addresses, parking ticket numbers or credit card numbers is encrypted using the highest level
of industry standard encryption. Public access will include access to current citation status, including
status of contested citations, due dates, original fine amount, late charges, information on how to
contest a citation, how to show proof of correction for correctable violations, how to submit claims of
indigence prior to a hearing, and addresses for paying in person or by mail.

Page 10

S&nbsp;
35 of&nbsp;312


--- page 36 ---
P. IVR and Web Payment Systems - Payment by Credit Card - Through the Interactive Voice
Response (IVR) System, and through the pticket.com web site, Contractor will accept credit card
payments via Visa, MasterCard and Discover. The systems authorize each transaction while the
caller is on the phone or online. Payees are given an authorization number or email confirmation to
confirm their charge. The IVR system and the pticket.com web payment system both automatically
update the citation database with the payment immediately. Credit Card monies will be paid to a
Contractor bank account and reconciled monthly. Customer will receive a credit card postlog which
shows in detail which citations were paid and for what amount, along with the deposit slip from the
bank or the ACH deposit email showing that these funds have been deposited into the Customer's
account. Should there be any charge backs to a merchant account, the funds are pulled directly
from the Contractor master account and the citation will be reactivated, much like a bounced check.
The violator will be sent a notice and will then proceed to DMV hold. Contractor will provide all
services regarding reconciliation, reactivation of charge backs, etc. The Customer will not be
involved in the daily processing. ‘

Q. Administrative Adjudication Processing - Contractor will provide for the processing of requests
for contesting citations, allowing for Customer processing of administrative reviews, tracking and
monitoring all relevant dates on an automated system, mailing timely notification to respondents
regarding the status of their claims, and scheduling of administrative hearings. All Administrative

_ Adjudication information entered into the system will be done in real time and linked to existing
database information to ensure proper tracking of relevant dates, mailing names and addresses and
other pertinent information, Administrative Review requests will be entered within 2 business days of
receipt. Adjudication documents will be stored for 2 years from their activity date and then shredded.
Contractor will notify Customer of citations that have been found Not Liable that need refunds, so
the Customer can issue the refund. Contractor will schedule combined San Mateo County Hearings
up to three (3) weeks in advance, according to citizen selection by location and day of week in one
of the San Mateo County locations. Hearings may be scheduled manually if requested. Contractor
will print and mai} (by first class mail) customized hearing notification letters to Customer and
respond to inquiries from Customer and the public regarding date of hearing, mailing date, location
of hearing and directions to hearing location. Contractor will provide the capability to use customized
text, such as liable reason codes, in letters for Customer and re-send letters should changes or
reschedules occur. Contractor agrees to provide all information required under the Vehicle Code ina
timely manner at no additional cost to the Customer should an appeal be made to the Superior
Court.

R. Paperless Appeals (eAppealsPRO & Scanning) — Contractor will provide online appeal capability
for the public to appeal their citations online. Contractor will provide the scanning of all mailed-in
appeal documents and electronic storage of those documents. Contractor will provide an online
application to access the appeals, which will be searchable and sortable. Contractor will keep an
electronic history of processed appeals for at least two years.

S. Independent Hearing Examiner Services — Contractor will contract with Independent Third Party
Hearing Examiners to provide fair and impartial hearings for Customer and the public. Contractor
will provide a monthly report of hearing results by citation number. The Independent Third Party
Hearing Examiners will meet all training, education and other requirements specified in the
California Vehicle Code which apply to the performance of administrative hearings.

T. Online Inquiry Access and Support for Customers’ Staff - Contractor will provide access to the
parking citation database via’'a web page using a secure log-on procedure. Customer shall be
provided access to their own database and inquiry-only access to databases for the other County
Agencies. This access includes citation inquiry by citation number, license plate number, full or
partial name and VIN (includes citation status, history status, administrative adjudication status,
notes, etc.), the ability to enter and view NOTES, post dismissals/payments, view daily deposits
made at Contractor's facility and view daily file transfers sent from the handheld ticket writer
software and received at Contractor's facility. A “NOTES” feature will allow authorized personnel to
easily enter comments for a particular citation or license plate to be viewed by other inquiry function
users. Contractor's technical staff will provide support during normal business hours. Technical
support will be provided for any communication or logon problems as well as immediate technical
support when problems arise in the uploading, downloading and transferring of files.

U. ICS Collection Service — Special Collections — Contractor will transfer outstanding citations (DMV
No-Holds, DMV Transfer of Ownership Releases, Non-California plates, citations delinquent over 90
days) and any other citations deemed as delinquent citations by Customer into the ICS system on a
weekly basis. Up to two collection letters will be mailed for each ICS account requesting payment.
Delinquent accounts will be sent to a credit reporting agency on a weekly basis. Paid accounts will
be reported to the credit reporting agency weekly. Payments will be processed daily and deposited
to the Customer's regular citation processing bank account. The Contractor’s Customer Service
Center will handle all ICS related calls through a special toll-free number dedicated to ICS accounts.
Monthly reporting will show all accounts moved to the ICS system and all payments received due to
ICS efforts.

V. Franchise Tax Board Offset Program — Contractor will combine citations by license number for
total amount due, eliminate corporate names, retrieve SSN’s by name from a 3rd party, combine
accounts by SSN, mail required FTB letters in advance of placing accounts at FTB, process
payments generated by the FTB process, receive phone calls generated by the FTB process,
provide all systems and operational procedures required for the FTB process, and provide complete
reporting and reconciliation for the FTB process. Customer will be required to complete required
FTB paperwork and forms (with Contractor's assistance), establish a SWIFT account with the FTB,
and provide whatever assistance may be required to work with the FTB regarding the FTB process.

e Privacy and Security of Customer Data - Contractor agrees to keep all Customer data private
and secure and will not share, sell, or otherwise access the Customer data for reasons other
than the normal processing of parking citations or as.otherwise required by law.

e System Backups - All systems will be backed up daily to insure safety of data in the event of a
power outage or natural disaster. All backup data should be transferred and stored off-site for
disaster recovery.

subcontracted, and the name of the private or public agency which shall perform the work.

e Vehicle Code Compliance - Contractor will comply with all requirements of the California
Vehicle Code in regard to processing and adjudication of citation records sent by the issuing
agency during the entire term of this Agreement, including extensions if any.

SUBJECT:
Commercial Property Management – Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a three-year contract with Prodesse Property Group to manage City-owned properties in the Downtown with a 
minimum annual service fee the greater of $12,000, or 6% of collected monthly gross income; and authorize the City 
Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.  
BACKGROUND:
The City owns and manages eight commercial properties in the Downtown. A+Mail Boxes & More, Beard Papa’s, Cold 
Stone Creamery, Fletch’s, and Red Giant Coffee are tenants at the Main Street Garage. Rise Pizzeria and Next Level Sports 
are retail and office tenants at the Transit Center, and the Century Theaters is the long-term ground lessee on the block of 
B Street between 2nd and 3rd Avenues. The Downtown commercial property management contract excludes the ground 
lease with Century Theater, as it is managed internally by staff. 
Since November 2012, the City contracted with Capital Realty, Inc for rent collection, property management, landlord 
representation, brokerage services and lease negotiations for the Downtown commercial properties. The contract was 
originally for a 3-year term with several extension options. The final extension expired in June 2020. In January 2020, the 
City issued a request for proposals for commercial property management services. The City received several competitive 
proposals.  However, due to the pandemic, the City delayed the section process and extended the contract with Capital 
Realty to December 2020. 
After resuming the selection process in August, staff selected Prodesse Property Group to be the commercial property 
manager for the City due to their extensive property management knowledge, customer service experience, and proposed 
contract rates. Headquartered in Foster City, Prodesse Property Group has over 26 years of experience in property 
management and specializes in providing property management services. Prodesse has extensive residential investment 
property and over 250,000 square feet of retail, light industrial, medical-dental, and office property throughout the Bay 
Area. Michael Pierce, President, and Dean Isaacs, Commercial Property Manager, are the principals of the company. The 
term of the contract will be initially for three years with one, two-year option to extend. The contract can be terminated 
with a 30-day notice. 
Prodesse Property Group was the most competitive in terms of costs of the RFP submittals received. For property 
management services, Prodesse Property Group proposals to charge the City the greater of 6% of monthly rent collection 
or a minimum of $1,000 per month. Due to COVID-19, Council approved a fifty percent rent reduction for all the tenants. 
Thus, in the immediate future, the minimum monthly fees will be $1,000. In addition to their share of the rents, Prodesse 
Property Group will also receive leasing fees for new tenants of 6.0% of the total base rent for lease years 1 and 2; 4.0% of 
the total base rent for lease years 3, 4 and 5; and 3.0% of the total base rent for lease years 6 through 10.  These fees 
40 of 312

--- page 41 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
would be shared on a 50/50 basis with any procuring brokers.  For current tenants, they will receive a lease renewal fee of 
$1,000 for each lease that is renegotiated and/or renewed. They will also be eligible for construction management fees for 
tenant improvements they oversee equal to 5.0% of the total construction costs for any projects that exceed $25,000. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The minimum annual fee for the service is $12,000. However, once full rents are being paid again, the contract fees are 
estimated to be $16,000 per year.  Prodesse will also be able to charge additional fees related to construction 
management, brokerage fees and lease renewals. The management fees are deducted from the lease payments remitted 
to the City. Commercial lease revenues are deposited in the Downtown Parking fund and are used to support the 
Downtown cleaning contract and maintenance of the parking garages.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
PROPERTY MANAGEMENT

Collect monthly rents from tenants and remit to the City, serve delinquency notices and assist 
the City with tenant eviction processes, whether for nonpayment of rent or violation of lease 
provision(s).

Serve as the primary contact for all tenants in the properties, and maintain a relationship with 
each tenant to better know their needs and/or concerns, and to ensure tenant compliance with 
lease terms and conditions.  

Represent the City in all matters relating to each tenant, under  current lease agreement.

Address any tenant issues with leases, building management, cleanliness and/or occupied 
spaces.

CONSULTANT will walk the exteriors of the properties on a weekly basis (and internally once a 
quarter, after lease-required notices to the tenants), to ensure the maintenance of the 
properties, making sure retail areas are safe and sanitary, and if vacant, show well, and 
notifying the City of any necessary repairs either within the premises,  in the common areas of 
the Garage and Transit Center, and immediate surrounding areas.

Oversee any maintenance work pre-approved by the City, including ensuring all contractors 
have City-approved licenses and insurance coverage, and pay prevailing wages if required.

Report the utility meter readings on a monthly basis, and report the same to City staff.

Provide 24-hour response to any emergency situations, reporting such events to the City by the 
next business day at the latest.

Facilitate and manage execution of lease extensions, amendments, reassignments, renewals 
and terminations with prior approval of the City.
LEASING

Advertise vacancies at the properties and on commercial property listing sites, and prepare all 
necessary marketing collateral.

Screen applicants for market competitiveness, compatibility of use,  check credits, and 
references.

Provide guidance to the City on fair market rent and tenant selection.


for conformity to those negotiations.

Review and make recommendation to City leases .
FINANCIAL


rent, CAM and percentage rent income would be deposited into this account, and the net cash 
flow from the properties, following payment of all expenses and withholding the $2,500.00 
reserve amount would be deposited into one of the City’s bank accounts each month.

Provide monthly bank statements and reconciliations to the City by the 15th or sooner day of the 
following month.

SUBJECT:
Central Park Tennis Court Garage Repair – Contract Change Order
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Contract Change Order #2 to the contract with Newton Construction and Management, Inc. in the amount of 
$279,903.18 for a new contract total of $1,030,197.44; increase the contingency reserve by $25,000 for a total 
contingency amount of $100,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the contract in substantially the 
form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Central Park Tennis Court Garage has served the San Mateo downtown community for sixty (60) years. It is a concrete 
structure that has 132 underground parking spaces on a single level and six (6) tennis courts on the roof level. The 
structure currently shows major deterioration throughout. A structural assessment was performed during 2019 that 
identified necessary repairs to the components of the garage structure in order to extend the estimated useful life of the 
garage by ten years. In August 2020, City Council awarded a construction contract to Newton Construction, Inc. to perform 
repairs to the Central Park Tennis Court Garage in the amount of $747,831.76. During August 2020, Change Order No. 1 
was issued in the amount of $2,462.50 for additional asbestos testing prior to the start of construction. 
The scope of work was established based on record drawings for the facility and field investigation by ZFA Structural 
Engineers, the structural engineer retained to design seismic improvements to the garage.  After the start of construction, 
the contractor identified that the upper surface of the garage requiring demolition and replacement was significantly 
thicker than presented in the record drawings, likely due to historic overlays and repairs.  Two other revisions are part of 
this change order, one to install a higher quality tennis court surfacing that will provide greater longevity and safety of the 
surface and the other to install lines for pickleball on all the courts.
For Change Order No. 2, the increased demolition cost is $187,882.78 and the surfacing and line installation cost is 
$92,020.40, for a total of $279,903.18.
Public Works staff recommends these changes and approval of this change order. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds in the Central Park Garage Repairs project to fund this change order.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
53 of 312

CITY OF SAN MATEO
15301.)

SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade Engineering Design Services During Construction – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the agreement with HDR Engineering, Inc. for additional engineering services during 
construction for the third construction package of the Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project in an 
amount not-to-exceed $12,273,376; approve a contingency reserve in the amount of $2,244,000; and authorize the Public 
Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the 
contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The City of San Mateo (City) is currently under a Regional Water Quality Control Board Cease and Desist Order requiring 
improvements to its collection system and Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) to eliminate sanitary sewer overflows 
and unauthorized discharges of untreated or partially treated wastewater to San Francisco Bay. The Clean Water Program 
includes several capital improvement projects that are currently under design and are intended to comply with the Cease 
and Desist Order. Specifically, the WWTP Upgrade and Expansion Project (Project) consists of new facilities, including a 
headworks, primary clarifiers, secondary treatment basins, membrane filtration, and a dedicated wet weather treatment 
train. 
On June 17, 2019, Council approved an agreement with HDR Engineering (HDR), the design engineer of record for the 
Project, to provide engineering services during construction for Package 1, the first of three construction packages. HDR’s 
negotiated fee for Package 1 was $450,221. On June 15, 2020, an amendment with HDR was approved by Council for 
Package 2 of the Project at a negotiated fee of $419,830.
For Package 3, HDR submitted an initial proposal for services during construction of $16,441,643. Staff conducted a 
comprehensive review of the proposed scope of work and eliminated tasks that overlapped and are covered through the 
construction management services and optimized the level of effort for efficiencies in delivery. This review and further 
negotiations resulted in a reduced scope of work and a final fee of $12,273,376, with a cost reduction of $4,168,267. Staff 
believe this fee to be reasonable for the effort and expertise required and recommends amending the agreement with 
HDR for Package 3 engineering services during construction. This amendment will bring the total fee of the agreement 
with HDR for all three construction packages to $13,143,427 as summarized in Table 1. 
A contingency amount of $2,244,000 is recommended to cover modifications to scope items that may be needed to 
complete the work. This amount includes $1,744,000 for known scope items that require additional coordination and 
definition and would be approved later; and $500,000 for unknown scope items. A preliminary list of scope items 
accounted for in the contingency reserve is summarized in Table 2. Construction of Package 3 is anticipated to be complete 
in September 2024.

BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are currently available in the Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project to award the 
services during construction for Package 3. However, the total Project costs (inclusive of engineering, planning, design, 
permitting, insurance and construction) are expected to be over budget. The forecasted cost variance may be alleviated 
over the remainder of the Project by unspent contingencies and allowances encumbered in the three Project construction 
packages. In addition, staff has re-evaluated a number of sewer collection system projects that are anticipated to offset 
this cost overrun. Staff will continue to closely monitor costs and potential changes, and work to manage the overall cost 
impact within the approved Clean Water Program budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). The PEIR was certified by City Council on June 6, 2016. In 
accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for implementation of 
the Clean Water Program. The City prepared an Addendum to the Final PEIR that were approved on July 16, 2018 
(Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the project evaluated in the PEIR and 
Addenda.

Exhibit A 
Scope of Services 
City of San Mateo Clean Water Program 
Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management  
Upgrade and Expansion Project 
Engineering Services during Construction for Guaranteed Maximum 
Price-3 (GMP-3) 
The following scope of work involves engineering services during construction of GMP-3 (balance of 
plant, administration building, and maintenance warehouse) package for the City of San Mateo (City) 
Clean Water Program (CWP) Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management Upgrade and 
Expansion Project (Project) located at the San Mateo/Estero Municipal Improvement District (EMID) 
Wastewater Treatment Plant. The vision of the City is to create a state-of-the-art, reliable wastewater 
treatment plant that will serve as “The Gem of the Bay.” 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION 
The Project includes the following upgrades and improvements: 
 
Realignment and extensions of onsite influent sewer force mains with flow metering to a new 
headworks facility. 
 
Four new covered rectangular primary clarifiers, with primary sludge pumps, scum pumps, 
and a primary effluent pumping station. 
 
Influent flow equalization basin (convert existing aeration basins) for use during peak wet 
weather flow conditions. Flow to the flow equalization basin will be by gravity and flow 
returned to the headworks will be pumped. 
 
BioActiflo® for wet weather treatment, consisting of a biological contact tank and high rate 
clarification process, along with associated mixers, aeration, blowers, and pumps. 
 
Chemical storage and feed facility. 
 
Biological nutrient removal (BNR) and membrane bioreactor (MBR) treatment facilities.  
 
Chlorination and dechlorination facility improvements. 
 
Below-grade gallery and tunnel system where some process equipment will be located and 
where process piping between facilities will be located. 
 
New two-story, 15,170-square-foot administration and treatment plant control building.

SCOPE OF SERVICES 
Task 1 – Project Management 
To provide a single point of communication representing the entire HDR design team, and to provide 
continuity from the design team throughout the duration of construction, HDR will provide project 
management services for the duration of the construction phase. Project management activities 
include the following: 
 
Preparing and submitting monthly progress reports that include a narrative of the work 
completed by task, upcoming work, project issues, budget and schedule status, potential 
scope or budget changes, and other important information. The project coordinator will assist 
with preparing monthly progress reports each month. 
61 of 312

--- page 62 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
3 
 
Preparing and submitting monthly invoices that document the man-hours and billing rates for 
staff for each task in the work breakdown structure (WBS), as well as overhead, profit, and 
direct costs. The current and previous billing period invoicing, as well as a summary of the 
budget spent, projected physical percent completed, and remaining cost to complete will be 
included in the monthly invoices.  
 
Providing cost accrual (which includes actual cost through the 15th of each month and 
projected cost through end of month) and progress update (which includes % physical 
complete by WBS task through the 15th of each month and projected progress through end 
of month) by the 25th of each month. 
 
Preparing subconsultant agreements, purchase orders, and contract amendments (to be 
performed by the project coordinator). 
This task also includes the regular activities performed by the HDR’s principal project manager, 
which include: 
 
Participating in monthly progress meetings with the City, CWP, and Contractor. 
 
Address key issues from resident engineer, deputy project manager, and other personnel 
that require principal project manager attention/action. 
 
Maintaining regular contact with City, CWP, and Construction Management leadership.  
This task also includes the regular activities performed by HDR’s deputy project manager, which 
include: 
 
Participating in monthly progress meetings with the City, CWP, and Contractor. 
 
Participating in weekly construction coordination meetings with the Contractor, and providing 
follow-up actions. 
 
Providing general coordination, and coordination of submittals and requests for information 
(RFIs). 
 
Preparing subconsultant contracts and amendments to the contract. 
 
Reviewing and approving monthly progress reports and invoices. 
 
Providing supporting technical information and materials as needed for regulatory meetings 
and public relation meetings during the construction phase.  
Project management for GMP-3 will commence on September 2, 2020, when project management 
for GMP-2 expires. Project management to support GMP-3 will be provided in two phases as noted 
in the Project Description section above and is budgeted as follows:

Task 2 – Meetings and Site Visits 
Subtask 2.1 – Meetings  
HDR will attend and participate in the following meetings during the construction period. 
Preconstruction Meeting 
HDR will attend and participate in the preconstruction meeting with the Contractor, CWP, 
and City prior to commencement of work at the site. It is assumed that the CWP will lead the 
meeting, prepare the required materials, and prepare and distribute meeting minutes. One 
HDR team member will attend the preconstruction meeting. 
Deliverables: None. 
Weekly Progress Meetings 
HDR’s resident engineer or deputy project manager will attend and participate in weekly 
progress meetings during construction. It is assumed the CWP will lead the meeting, prepare 
the required materials, and prepare and distribute meeting minutes.  
Follow-up telephone calls with the construction management team may be required to 
reconcile requests for information (RFIs) and submittals. 
The resident engineer’s attendance at weekly progress meetings is budgeted under Task 7. 
The deputy project manager’s attendance at weekly progress meetings is budgeted under 
Task 1. 
HDR will participate in selected weekly coordination meetings, at the request of the Owner’s 
Representative during construction via telephone or virtually via computer. The budget for 
this task is based on attendance at:

Subtask 2.2 – Site Visits 
The following site visits are anticipated: 
Periodic Site Visits from Design Team 
HDR’s team will provide members of the design team to make periodic site visits covering 
work such as geotechnical, structural, electrical, mechanical equipment placement, 
architectural, HVAC, instrumentation and control (I&C), site civil, landscape architecture and 
other technical disciplines related to key design issues.  
For each site visit, HDR will take photographs and will prepare a site visit report that 
documents the purpose of the site visit, the outcome and results of the site visit, a punch list 
of outstanding issues or items for correction, and ultimately a recommendation as to the 
pass/failure of the system/equipment based on the criteria outlined during the site visit.  
65 of 312

--- page 66 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
7 
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format with photos.  
Factory Testing 
HDR’s team will also witness the factory testing of major mechanical, electrical, and I&C 
equipment. It is assumed factory testing will be performed within the U.S. 
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format.  
Substantial Completion Visit 
HDR’s team will attend a site visit at the substantial completion project milestone identified 
by the CWP and Contractor. CWP will prepare a list of items to be completed or corrected. 
HDR’s team will review the list for concurrence, including the I&C system startup punch lists 
based on observations during onsite testing.  
HDR will take photographs and will prepare a site visit report that documents the purpose of 
the site visit, the outcome and results of the site visit, a punch list of outstanding issues or 
items for correction, and ultimately a recommendation as to the pass/failure of the 
system/equipment based on the criteria outlined during the site visit.  
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format.  
Final Site Visit 
The final site visit will involve reviewing the final work, assisting the CWP with preparing a 
punch list, reviewing and recommending substantial completion, and reviewing and 
recommending final inspection.  
HDR will take photographs and will prepare a site visit report that documents the purpose of 
the site visit, the outcome and results of the site visit, a punch list of outstanding issues or 
items for correction, and ultimately a recommendation as to the pass/failure of the 
system/equipment based on the criteria outlined during the site visit.  
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format.

Task 5 – Office Engineering Services for GMP-3 
Subtask 5.1 – Technical Submittals 
HDR will review the Contractor’s submittals, including shop drawings and operations and 
maintenance (O&M) manuals, as required by the technical specifications, for work related to HDR’s 
scope of design services. HDR will review and accept the Contractor’s submittals, such as shop 
drawings, product data, samples, and other data, for the limited purpose of checking for 
conformance with the design concept and the information expressed in the contract documents. This 
review will not include review of the accuracy or completeness of details, such as quantities, 
dimensions, weights or gauges, fabrication process, construction means or methods, coordination of 
the work with other trades, or construction safety precautions, all of which are the sole responsibility 
of the Contractor. Review of a specific item will not indicate that HDR has reviewed the entire 
assembly of which the item is a component. HDR will not be responsible for any deviations from the 
contract documents not brought to the attention of HDR in writing by the Contractor. HDR will not be 
required to review partial submissions nor those for which submissions of correlated items have not 
been received. 
The number of submittals was calculated based on 1.3 submittals per design drawing. Up to 6 
engineering hours are budgeted for each submittal. A 50 percent resubmission rate and up to 3 
engineering hours per resubmittal is also assumed. Deviations from the anticipated numbers of 
submittals/resubmittals may impact the total actual level of effort required for review of technical 
submittals.  An additional hour per initial submittal will be included for Task 5.1 in contingency to 
provide additional labor to review technical submittals, if needed. Use of contingency for additional 
submittal review requires City authorization.  
Please note that the hours for the onsite resident engineer to review submittals are covered under 
Task 7.The following HDR’s hours for review of technical submittals were reduced and applied to the 
resident engineer: 

Calendar Year 2020: 20-hour reduction.

Calendar Year 2021: 70-hour reduction.

Calendar Year 2022: 70-hour reduction.
Deliverables: 

Up to 2,090 submittals and 1,045 resubmittals (based on 1,608 drawing count).

Subtask 5.2 –RFIs and Clarifications 
HDR will review RFIs received from the Contractor, and will evaluate the acceptability of substitute 
materials and equipment.  
HDR will answer questions and provide written interpretations of the requirements of the contract 
documents. Such clarifications and interpretations will be consistent with the intent of, and 
reasonably inferable from, the contract drawings and specifications. 
The number of RFIs/design clarifications was calculated based on 1.25 RFI/design clarification per 
design drawing. Up to 4 engineering hours per RFI was assumed. Deviations from the anticipated 
numbers of RFIs/design clarifications may impact the total actual level of effort required for RFI 
responses and preparation of design clarifications.   
Please note that the hours for the onsite resident engineer to review RFIs and clarifications are 
covered under Task 5.  
Deliverables: 

Up to 2,010 RFIs (based on 1,608 drawing count).

Subtask 5.4 – Documentation Management 
A document management system (Procore) will be used to manage, track, and store relevant 
documents between the Contractor, CWP, and City. Procore will be used exclusively to document 
and transmit submittal reviews, RFI responses, correspondence, inspection and testing reports, and 
other project-related documentation.  
HDR will receive, internally distribute, track, and return shop drawings, other submittals, and 
documents from the Contractor in accordance with the procedures set forth in the project’s 
construction management plan.  
The budget for this task is entirely for the Project Coordinator and assumes 24 hours per week for 
Phase 1 (152 weeks) and 16 hours per week for Phase 2 (39 weeks), plus an additional 40 hours for 
close-out duties. 
Deliverables: Procore data and reports. 
Subtask 5.5 – LEED Certification 
The LEED Certification effort will be led by the Integral Group (IG). HDR, RHAA, the City, and BTA 
and their subconsultants will be responsible for LEED credit documentation associated with their 
respective scope of work.  
The following assumptions apply to the scope described below:  
 
LEED consulting services apply to the Administration Building and site within the LEED 
Boundary only 
 
Project Schedule (Administration Building) April 2021 – September 2023  
 
Rating System Type: LEED v4 NC 
 
Rating System Target: Silver minimum 
 
See IG Scope of Work in Appendix A for additional scope, assumptions and exclusions. 
IG’s approach is tailored to the specific needs and sustainability goals of the project. When 
designing the LEED strategy, we work collaboratively with the owner, architect, and all relevant 
consultants to ensure that project goals are aligned with the LEED scorecard. We identify synergies 
between the project design and the rating system, including the evaluation of LEED v4.1 credit 
upgrades where applicable, to maximize credit opportunities. Throughout design and construction, 
IG works closely with the project team to ensure the strategy is met.  
LEED Certification subtasks include the following: 
 
Submit Design Credits to GBCI for Design Review Submittal, issuing review comments to 
respective design team members, and managing the resubmittal of design credits.  
 
Host a LEED construction kick-off with CMAR Contractor and major trades.  
 
Review Contractor’s LEED Action Plan

Subtask 5.6 – Furniture, Fixture, and Equipment (FFE) Allowance 
BTA and their subconsultants will assist the City in the selection and procurement of FFE for the 
administration building. Assistance will be limited to office furniture, workstations, and office 
equipment.  Selection and procurement of audio visual equipment is not included. FFE assistance 
services include: 
 
Meetings with City to determine applicable design criteria – up to three meetings.  
 
Site visit to verify applicable field conditions to ensure proper layout of systems and 
freestanding furniture.  
 
Preparing preliminary and final furniture space plan. 
 
Selection of new furniture finishes including panel fabric, paint, plastic laminate, and base 
trim.  
 
Production of furniture specifications and installation documents.  
Deliverables: Administration building FFE specifications and installation documents. 
Task 6 – Close-Out Activities 
Subtask 6.1 – Electronic O&M (eOM) Manual (Contingency) 
HDR may provide assistance to the City in developing an electronic O&M manual for the Project.  
However, the City is uncertain at this time exactly what HDR’s scope of services for the eOM may be 
needed.  Therefore, HDR’s draft scope of services and budget will be held in contingency until such 
time these services are required.  The draft scope of services for the eOM are included in 
Attachment A-3.  
Subtask 6.2 - Startup/Commissioning Assistance 
Process Startup/Commissioning Assistance 
HDR will assist the CWP, Contractor, and City in the startup and commissioning of new unit 
processes and auxiliary systems.  The Contractor shall lead the Startup and Commissioning 
development.  The CWP will oversee clean water checkout of new unit processes and auxiliary 
systems and HDR will drive the process startup at the plant.  HDR shall lead the process portion of 
the Startup and Commissioning process with close coordination with the Contractor and CWP.  
Acting as Owner’s Engineer during Startup/Commissioning, HDR will perform the following tasks: 
Startup and Commissioning Plan 
o 
HDR will communicate expectations to CWP and the Contractor on the structure and 
content of the Startup and Commissioning Plan.  
73 of 312

--- page 74 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
15 
o 
HDR will provide a template of a Startup and Commissioning Plan to CWP and the 
Contractor for their completion. 
o 
HDR will review and comment on drafts of the Startup and Commissioning Plan that are 
prepared by CWP and the Contractor.  
o 
HDR will provide its approval of the Startup and Commissioning Plan when it meets the 
project’s needs. 
o 
HDR will review and approve all modifications to the Startup and Commissioning Plan. 
Equipment Commissioning 
During the Pre-Functional Testing phase of each process level, HDR will monitor progress of 
activities as per the approved Startup and Commissioning Plan. It will be the responsibility of 
CWP and the Contractor to successfully complete all activities of the Pre-Functional Testing 
phase.  
HDR will take a more active role in Equipment Commissioning beginning in the Functional 
Testing Phase. During this phase, and all subsequent phases, HDR will verify successful 
completion of all equipment and system test requirements in the approved Startup and 
Commissioning Plan and notify the CWP and Contractor when each system has been 
successfully completed. The decision to move to the next phase will be jointly made by the 
City, CWP and HDR. 
HDR will develop and provide workshops on plant-wide startup, commissioning, and 
performance testing plans.  
The Equipment Commissioning phase will conclude with the successful completion of a 
System Test, which will loop clean water throughout all the new assets of the project. Details 
of these requirements will be in the approved Startup and Commissioning Plan. HDR will 
confirm when the requirements have been met, and the decision to move to the next phase 
will be jointly made by the City, CWP and HDR.  
Startup 
During Startup Phase, the treatment processes will be acclimated to a point where they are 
ready to begin the Performance Test. City operations staff will operate the new processes 
during Startup.  
During the Startup Phase, HDR will provide onsite operations specialists to: 
 
Verify that the Startup activities identified in the Startup and Commissioning Plan are 
being completed. 
 
Provide assistance to City operations staff. 
 
Troubleshoot issues as they arise. 
74 of 312

--- page 75 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
16 
Performance Test 
During the Performance Test, HDR will provide engineers and operations specialists to 
monitor and analyze the technical data of the new processes. The data will have already 
been identified in the approved Startup and Commissioning Plan.  
HDR will provide its recommendation to the City of successful completion of the Performance 
Test when it determines that all requirements have been met.  
HDR will also provide support to City operations staff during the Performance Test.  
During the startup and performance testing period which is scheduled to occur between May 
24, 2023 and October 17, 2023 (23 weeks including a 2 week buffer period) HDR will provide 
the services of a full-time operations specialist and half-time process mechanical engineer 
and electrical engineer to drive the startup and performance testing of the new unit 
processes and auxiliary systems.  This startup and performance testing assistance includes 
flexible scheduling to cover day and night shifts for 24 hour plant operational periods. 
Processes Covered Under Startup and Commissioning 
HDR’s startup and commissioning operations specialists will support startup at the individual 
process unit level and at the facility level to make sure processes work well together. It is

Scope of Services 
City of San Mateo Clean Water Program 
Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management  
Upgrade and Expansion Project 
Engineering Services during Construction 
The following scope of work involves engineering services during construction for the City of San 
Mateo (City) Clean Water Program (CWP) Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management 
Upgrade and Expansion Project (Project) located at the San Mateo/Estero Municipal Improvement 
District (EMID) Wastewater Treatment Plant. The vision of the City is to create a state-of-the-art, 
reliable wastewater treatment plant that will serve as “The Gem of the Bay.”  Brown and Caldwell 
(BC) is a subconsultant to HDR for the instrumentation and controls (I&C) scope of the design. 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION 
The Project includes the following upgrades and improvements: 

Realignment and extensions of on-site influent sewer force mains with flow metering to a
new headworks facility.

Four new covered rectangular primary clarifiers, with primary sludge pumps, scum pumps,
and a primary effluent pumping station.

Influent flow equalization basin (convert existing aeration basins) for use during peak wet
weather flow conditions. Flow to the flow equalization basin will be by gravity and flow
returned to the headworks will be pumped.

BioActiflo® for wet weather treatment, consisting of a biological contact tank and high rate
clarification process, along with associated mixers, aeration, blowers and pumps.

Chemical storage and feed facility.

Biological nutrient removal (BNR) and membrane bioreactor (MBR) treatment facilities.

Chlorination and dechlorination facility improvements.

Below-grade gallery and tunnel system where some process equipment will be located and
where process piping between facilities will be located.

New two-story, 15,170-square-foot administration and treatment plant control building.
81 of 312

--- page 82 ---
20-10075318. 
10/6/20 
2 
 
Odor control for the new headworks and primary clarifiers. 
 
New 4,000-square-foot warehouse. 
 
Site work. 
 
Landscaping. 
The Project is being delivered using a Construction Manager at Risk (CMAR) delivery method. 
Construction of the Project is separated into three guaranteed maximum price (GMP) packages, as 
follows: 
 
GMP-1 - Demolition, Mass Excavation, Perimeter Shoring, SEMS, Stormwater 
 
GMP-2 - Piles 
 
GMP-3 - Balance of Plant, Administration Building, and Maintenance Warehouse

Subtask 5.1 – Technical Submittals 
BC will review the Contractor’s submittals, including shop drawings and operations and maintenance 
(O&M) manuals, as required by the technical specifications, for work related to BC’s scope of design 
services. BC will review and accept the Contractor’s submittals, such as shop drawings, product 
data, samples, and other data, for the limited purpose of checking for conformance with the design 
concept and the information expressed in the contract documents. This review will not include review 
of the accuracy or completeness of details, such as quantities, dimensions, weights or gauges, 
fabrication process, construction means or methods, coordination of the work with other trades, or 
construction safety precautions, all of which are the sole responsibility of the Contractor. Review of a 
specific item will not indicate that BC has reviewed the entire assembly of which the item is a 
component. BC will not be responsible for any deviations from the contract documents not brought to 
the attention of BC in writing by the Contractor. BC will not be required to review partial submissions 
nor those for which submissions of correlated items have not been received. 
The number of submittals was calculated based on 1.3 submittals per design drawing. Up to 6 
engineering hours are budgeted for each submittal. A 50 percent resubmission rate and up to 3 
engineering hours per resubmittal were also assumed. Deviations from the anticipated schedule or 
duration of construction, or increased numbers of submittals/resubmittals will materially affect the 
scope of these services and BC’s compensation and will constitute additional services.  
BC will provide responses to submittals within the timelines stipulated in Section 01 33 00 1.3F, 
which are typically 20 working days for equipment, and 40 working days for detailed I&C submittals 
(control panels, wiring diagrams, PLC programming, etc.), assuming that HDR provides submittals to 
BC within one day of receipt from the Contractor. 
BC’s staffing for reviewing submittals, responding to RFIs and supporting the project will typically 
consist of the I&C design engineers responsible for design of the project (J. Cook, P. Murphy), the 
PM who also has a background in wastewater I&C systems (A. Hansen), and subject matter experts 
in Profibus networking implementation (D. White). Other staff may be used or substituted at BC’s 
discretion to adequately support the project needs. 
Deliverables: 
 
Up to 281 submittals and 141 resubmittals (based on 216 drawing count).

The following overall assumptions support the scope of services for engineering services during 
construction of the City’s Project. 


packages. 


the beginning of the Scope of Services. 
 
HDR will be coordinating all project workflows related to submittals, RFIs, and construction-
related responses.  BC has not budgeted for training, use, or administration of project 
controls software applications (e.g. Procore, etc.) 
 
BC will only be involved in the I&C design related aspects of GMP 3. 
 
For planning travel, we have assumed HDR will provide 3-weeks notice for scheduling site 
visits 
 
The City will contract directly with an owner representative (OR)/construction management 
(CM) services firm. It is assumed the OR/CM will provide construction management and daily 
on-site inspection for all construction trades, and monitor compliance with the contract 
documents and quality assurance of the work on the Project. 
 
General responsibilities for the OR/CM, HDR, Contractor, and City are as defined in the 
Responsibility Assignment Matrix dated April 18, 2018. 
 
BC will not be responsible for the means or methods of the Contractor, nor shall BC be 
responsible for the Contractor’s failure to perform in accordance with the contract 
documents. Management of these activities will be the responsibility of the City and the 
OR/CM. 
 
BC will not be responsible for the monitoring or review of the Contractor’s cost and schedule 
performance during construction. 
 
BC will not be responsible for providing construction contract administration, including 
processing of monthly payment requests from the Contractor, Contractor schedule updates 
and revisions, providing correspondence to the Contractor, receiving correspondence from 
the Contractor, and maintaining correspondence files.

Exhibit A-2.2 
Scope of Services 
City of San Mateo Clean Water Program 
Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management  
Upgrade and Expansion Project 
Engineering Services during Construction 
The purpose of this Scope of Services is to provide architectural and engineering support services 
during construction for the City of San Mateo (City) Clean Water Program (CWP) Nutrient Removal 
and Wet Weather Flow Management Upgrade and Expansion Project (Project) located at the San 
Mateo/Estero Municipal Improvement District (EMID) Wastewater Treatment Plant.  
The scope of services outlined herein recognizes that the project is being delivered using a 
Construction Manager at Risk (CMAR) delivery method and that Burks Toma Architects, Inc. (BTA) 
will be subconsultants to HDR Engineers. The budgets herein are based on a construction schedule 
outlined below.  
The following project description and major task listing is based on the Exhibit A Scope of Services 
outlined in HDR’s agreement with the City. 
PROJECT DESCRIPTION 
The Project includes the following upgrades and improvements: 

Realignment and extensions of on-site influent sewer force mains with flow metering to a new
headworks facility.

Four new covered rectangular primary clarifiers, with primary sludge pumps, scum pumps, and a
primary effluent pumping station.

Influent flow equalization basin (convert existing aeration basins) for use during peak wet
weather flow conditions. Flow to the flow equalization basin will be by gravity and flow returned
to the headworks will be pumped.

BioActiflo® for wet weather treatment, consisting of a biological contact tank and high rate
clarification process, along with associated mixers, aeration, blowers and pumps.

Chemical storage and feed facility.

Biological nutrient removal (BNR) and membrane bioreactor (MBR) treatment facilities.

Chlorination and dechlorination facility improvements.
92 of 312

--- page 93 ---
20-10075318 
10/6/20 
2 
 
Below-grade gallery and tunnel system where some process equipment will be located and 
where process piping between facilities will be located. 
 
New two-story, 15,170-square-foot administration and treatment plant control building. 
 
Odor control for the new headworks and primary clarifiers. 
 
New 4,000-square-foot warehouse. 
 
Site work. 
 
Landscaping. 
The Project is being delivered using a Construction Manager at Risk (CMAR) delivery method. 
Construction of the Project is separated into three guaranteed maximum price (GMP) packages, as 
follows: 
 
GMP-1 - Demolition, Mass Excavation, Perimeter Shoring, SEMS, Stormwater – No involvement 
by BTA. 
 
GMP-2 – Piles - No involvement by BTA. 
 
GMP-3 - Balance of Plant, Administration Building, and Maintenance Warehouse 
o 
BTA’s and subconsultant design services during construction for GMP-3 are based upon 
the Contractor’s Project Construction Overall Duration schedule dated January 28, 2019 
showing an overall construction duration of 143 weeks (September 1, 2020, through May 
31, 2023). In summary, the Contractor’s schedule can be broken down as follows:

SCOPE OF SERVICES 
Task 1 – Project Management 
BTA will provide project management services for the Administration Building team for the duration 
of the construction phase. Project management activities include the following: 
 
Preparing and submitting monthly progress reports that include a narrative of the work 
completed by BTA and subconsultants by task, upcoming work, project issues, budget and 
schedule status, potential scope or budget changes, and other important information.

staff and subconsultants for each task. The current and previous billing period invoicing, as 
well as a summary of the budget spent, projected physical percent completed, and remaining 
cost to complete will be included in the monthly invoices.  
 
Providing cost accrual (which includes actual cost through the 15th of each month and 
projected cost through end of month) and progress update (which includes % physical 
complete by WBS task through the 15th of each month and projected progress through end

Subtask 2.2 –Site Visits 
The following site visits are anticipated: 
Periodic Site Visits from Design Team 
BTA’s team will make periodic site visits covering work such as architectural, structural, 
electrical, HVAC, mechanical and other technical disciplines related to key design issues. 
Site visits may be conducted via Video Conference, if applicable.    
For each site visit, BTA will take photographs or review photographs from on-site personnel, 
and will prepare a site visit report that documents the purpose of the site visit, the outcome 
and results of the site visit, a punch list of outstanding issues or items for correction, and 
ultimately a recommendation as to the pass/failure of the system/equipment based on the 
criteria outlined during the site visit. BTA subconsultants’ scope for Site Visits are described 
in their respective scopes, see Appendix A. 
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format with photos.  
Structural Observation 
See IDA Structural Engineer’s scope description. 
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format.  
Substantial Completion Visit 
BTA’s team will attend a site visit at the substantial completion project milestone identified by 
the CWP and Contractor. CWP will prepare a list of items to be completed or corrected. 
BTA’s team will review the list for concurrence.
