Subtask 5.1 – Technical Submittals 
BTA will review the Contractor’s submittals, including shop drawings and product data, as required 
by the technical specifications, for work related to BTA’s scope of design services. BTA will review 
and accept the Contractor’s submittals, such as shop drawings, product data, samples, and other 
data, for the limited purpose of checking for conformance with the design concept and the 
information expressed in the contract documents. This review will not include review of the accuracy 
or completeness of details, such as quantities, dimensions, weights or gauges, fabrication process, 
construction means or methods, coordination of the work with other trades, or construction safety 
precautions, all of which are the sole responsibility of the Contractor. Review of a specific item will 
not indicate that BTA has reviewed the entire assembly of which the item is a component. BTA will 
not be responsible for any deviations from the contract documents not brought to the attention of 
BTA in writing by the Contractor. BTA will not be required to review partial submissions nor those for 
which submissions of correlated items have not been received. 
The number of submittals was calculated based on 1.3 submittals per design drawing. Up to 67 
engineering hours are budgeted for each submittal. A 50 percent resubmission rate and up to 3 
engineering hours per resubmittal were also assumed. Deviations from the anticipated schedule or 
duration of construction, or increased numbers of submittals/resubmittals will materially affect the 
scope of these services and BTA’s compensation and will constitute additional services.  
Deliverables: 
 
Up to __164____ submittals and __82____ resubmittals (based on __126___ drawing count). 
Subtask 5.2 – RFIs and Clarifications 
BTA will review RFIs received from the Contractor, and will evaluate the acceptability of substitute 
materials and equipment.  
BTA will answer questions and provide written interpretations of the requirements of the contract 
documents. Such clarifications and interpretations will be consistent with the intent of, and 
reasonably inferable from, the contract drawings and specifications. 
The number of RFIs/design clarifications was calculated based on 1.25 RFI/design clarification per 
design drawing. Up to 4 engineering hours per RFI was assumed. Deviations from the anticipated 
schedule or duration of construction, or increased numbers of RFIs/design clarifications will 
materially affect the scope of these services and BTA’s compensation and will constitute additional 
services.

Subtask 5.3 – LEED Certification 
The LEED Certification effort will be led by Integral Group (IG).  HDR, Sundt, the City, IG, RHAA, 
HTG and BTA and their subconsultants will be responsible for LEED credit documentation 
associated with their respective scope of work.  
Key Assumptions  
The following assumptions apply to the scope described below:  
 
LEED consulting services apply to the Administration Building and site within the LEED 
Boundary only 
 
Project Schedule (Administration Building) April 2021 – September 2023  
 
Rating System Type: LEED v4 NC 
 
Rating System Target: Silver minimum 
See Integral Group Scope of Work in Appendix A for additional scope, assumptions and 
exclusions. 
Approach  
IG’s approach is tailored to the specific needs and sustainability goals of the project. When 
designing the LEED strategy, we work collaboratively with the owner, architect and all relevant 
consultants to ensure that project goals are aligned with the LEED scorecard. We identify synergies 
between the project design and the rating system, including the evaluation of LEED v4.1 credit 
upgrades where applicable, to maximize credit opportunities. Throughout design and construction, 
IG works closely with the project team to ensure the strategy is met.  
LEED Certification Sub-Tasks 
 
Coordinate completion and QC review of Design Phase Credits. Submission of credits to GBCI 
for Design Review Submittal, issuing review comments to respective design team members, and 
managing the resubmittal of design credits. 
 
 Host a LEED construction kick-off with GC and major trades.  
 
Review Contractor’s LEED Action Plan  
o 
It is the responsibility of the General Contractor to appoint a LEED point person to 
provide a plan of action to achieve all Construction LEED Credits, including but not 
limited to Construction Waste Management, SWPP/ESC, IAQ Plans, IAQ Testing/Flush 
out, and preliminary estimates of material types, costs and LEED metrics for the 
achievement of Materials credits.  
 
Review and markup GC’s Submittal Log at the outset of construction to indicate which 
submittals will be reviewed for LEED.  
 
Conduct LEED submittal reviews throughout CA. 
o 
Integral Group will review product data only, not shop drawings.  
o 
Submittal reviews as necessary to achieve targeted LEED credits, not to exceed 70 total 
reviews.  
 
Review contractor’s quarterly LEED progress reports.  
 
Manage the documentation process for the preliminary and final LEED Construction Application.

Executive Summary 
Wastewater treatment processes are complex systems with many interconnecting streams and control 
systems. Therefore, process modeling tools are becoming essential for solving various problems and 
optimizing performance at wastewater treatment plants. Wastewater treatment plant models are used 
to track mass flows, to calculate conversion rates in unit processes, and to predict key performance 
indicators like effluent quality, sludge production, oxygen and chemical demand for different 
operational conditions.  
This proposal is prepared for the San Mateo Public Works Department for wastewater treatment 
process simulation software for the San Mateo Wastewater Treatment Plant. The objective of the 
project will be to develop a simulator for San Mateo’s wastewater treatment system so that the model 
can be used to 1) troubleshoot plant upsets and impact to effluent quality 2) support plant process 
optimization efforts and disaster recovery plans and 3) provide automated training to new operational 
staff. The proposal outlines a detailed project execution plan to help achieve the stipulated objectives.  
The first and second objectives of the project will be achieved by developing a mathematical model for 
the biological, chemical and physical treatment sections of the Sewage Treatment Plant in the GPS-X™ 
simulation platform.  GPS-X™ is a leading-edge dynamic simulation environment developed by 
Hydromantis to model the biological, chemical and physical processes at any wastewater treatment 
plant. GPS-X™ contains published activated sludge models like ASM1, ASM2d and ASM3 and extended 
advanced whole-plant models like Mantis2 to model two-step nitrification/denitrification, biological 
phosphorus removal, anaerobic digestion, pH/Alkalinity and chemical phosphorous removal. These 
models are widely used by engineers for accurate design, optimization and operation of wastewater 
treatment plants 
Hydromantis will work together with HDR and San Mateo’s project manager to assist in testing, 
troubleshooting and resolving issues. Hydromantis will provide support installation support and on-line 
training for engineering and operations staff members in the use of the model. 
Hydromantis will provide software license for the maximum of 5 concurrent users.  All licenses delivered 
will be annual, renewable licenses. 
Hydromantis is a Canadian, employee-owned company based in Hamilton, Ontario.  Our company is 
uniquely positioned in the wastewater simulation industry with the necessary technology and expertise 
to complete this project to the highest satisfaction of San Mateo.  Hydromantis is the only simulation 
company with proven experience creating mathematical models for engineering design and 
optimization (GPS-X™) that can also be combined with a custom operations-oriented interface for 
troubleshooting and training (SimuWorks™).   
We have over 30 years of experience as a leader in the wastewater modelling field, with over 10 years of 
experience providing realistic graphical model interfaces for operations personnel. Our knowledgeable 
103 of 312

--- page 104 ---
iii 
wastewater engineering and software programming staff will bring the experience of many similar, 
successfully completed projects to this new endeavor.  In particular, our recent projects to create 
wastewater treatment simulators with graphical interfaces for a) Greenville Utilities Commission, NC, 
USA, b) North Davis Sewer District, UT, USA, c) North Texas Municipal Water District, TX, USA, d) Pima 
County, AZ, USA, e) Regional Municipality of York, ON, Canada, f) City of Peterborough, ON, Canada g) 
Little Patuxent Solids Handling, MD, USA, h) Port Royal BJWSA, SC, USA, i) Beijing Drainage Group, 
Beijing, China  are similar to San Mateo proposed project.

Project Understanding 
Project Background 
The San Mateo San Mateo Wastewater Treatment Plant is a secondary treatment facility that can 
operate in normal mode with 2-stage Modified Ludzack-Ettinger (MLE) process and MBR process, or wet 
weather mode with MBR, a biological contact tank and an Actiflo Process. The design capacity of the 
plant is 60 MGD at peak-day, and is composed of the following process units: 
• 
Headworks receiving raw sewage and on-site return flows 
• 
Preliminary treatment (grit removal facility and screen facility) 
• 
Flow equalization to reduce storm peak flows 
• 
Secondary treatment – includes four parallel trains of BNR process and membrane tanks 
• 
Chemical phosphorus removal, using ferric chloride 
• 
Disinfection with chlorine 
• 
Biosolids handling facilities – includes primary sludge thickening, waste activated sludge (WAS) 
thickening and anerobic digestion 
• 
Dewatering centrifuge for digested solids 
• 
Final effluent discharge (with pumping station) 
San Mateo is interested in acquiring a leading-edge simulation-based software specialized for 
wastewater process modeling including biological simulations to help operations and optimization staff 
trouble shoot plant upset issues, train new operators, and aid in plant optimization efforts. The software 
will provide high accuracy and effective simulation capabilities to both engineers and wastewater 
operational staff. 
The use of a calibrated model of San Mateo’s wastewater plant processes, systems and equipment is 
expected to provide wastewater engineers and operators with advanced tools to: 
• 
Troubleshoot plant upsets and impacts on effluent quality 
• 
Aid in wet weather flow management 
• 
Provide automated training to new operational staff 
• 
Support plant process optimization efforts 
Scope of Services 
The main objectives of the proposed project are as listed below: 
1. To update the mathematical model for the San Mateo Wastewater Treatment Plant that was 
originally created in 2018.   The model will incorporate the new wet weather operating mode, as 
described to Hydromantis by HDR in August 2019. 
106 of 312

--- page 107 ---
2 
2. The mathematical model will be configured in the SimuWorks graphical interface, to be used by 
San Mateo operational staff, for day-to-day operational and troubleshooting advice, and for 
operator training.  It will have plant-specific, realistic graphical representations of the actual 
wastewater treatment system being simulated.  The model inputs will be restricted to typical 
operational parameters that operators would adjust at the real plant. 
3. To provide adequate software licensing for San Mateo staff to use the models as needed. 
4. To conduct training sessions to train San Mateo staff regarding the use of the model.  The goal 
of the training is to “train the trainers” so that San Mateo staff members can train others within 
the organization as needed. 
5. To provide on-going technical support and software maintenance, to refine the system, and 
ensure the smooth adoption of the modelling tools.

Project Methodology 
Project Activities 
In this section, we will describe our proven methodology for the scoping, development, construction and 
implementation of wastewater treatment models and graphical simulators for municipalities.  The 
following sections describe the work-plan for this project. 
Work Plan 
The following activities will be undertaken to achieve the objectives during this modelling project:

Task 1: Project Management 
In this activity regular communication through email and phone will be performed to coordinate 
activities and manage resources for timely completion of the project. Regular progress meeting will be 
held to discuss the progress of the project and identify critical items needing attention.  
Task 2: Kick-off Meeting 
The project will start with a kick-off meeting with HDR and San Mateo staff to discuss the scope and 
details of the project, and  
The focus of the kick-off meeting will be for Hydromantis to review the updated wet weather operation 
and to jointly discuss a set of simulation scenarios to be developed for the calibrated model.  Details 
about how the modelling software will ultimately deployed and licensed will also be discussed. 
108 of 312

--- page 109 ---
4 
Task 3: Update Model Wet Weather Operation 
Hydromantis will take the San Mateo GPS-X™ model originally created in 2018 and update the dry/wet 
weather operational models as described by HDR in August 2019.  The custom code for setting flow 
splitting, bypass pumping, clarifier operation, activated sludge tank operation and other flow control will 
be modified to match to the new approach.  Any other modifications to the GPS-X™ model required to 
support the new operation will be made at this time. 
Once built and calibrated, the model can be used to predict the effects of the biological growth 
processes and solids separation on conventional water quality parameters including cBOD5, COD, TKN, 
TSS, total NH3-N, NO2-N, NO3-N, total phosphorus, soluble phosphorus, pH/Alkalinity. The level of detail 
in the model will be equivalent or more than the International Water Association (IWA) family of 
activated sludge models (such as ASM1, ASM2d, ASM3, etc., which are all included in GPS-X™).  Model 
selection for the various plant processes will be based on consultations between Hydromantis, HDR and 
San Mateo staff. 
The process model will be able to execute both steady state and dynamic simulations and respond to 
changes to the input variables.  The process model will be predominantly mechanistic and can predict 
the performance of each individual process based on engineering principles.  For normal plant 
operation, the model can predict the effect of varying input or control variables such as chemical 
dosages, oxygen feed rates, increases in average daily flow, RAS and WAS flow rates, MLSS and/or SRT, 
wastewater temperature, influent quality, recycle ratio, accepting varying amounts of supernatant and 
septic waste and varying quality of raw sewage. 
Task 4: Scoping and Design of SimuWorks Interface 
Once the underlying GPS-X model has been finalized, Hydromantis with meet with HDR and San Mateo 
staff to scope out and design the SimuWorks interface.  Hydromantis will engage staff in scoping 
exercises designed to determine the most appropriate forms of model inputs and controls to be used.  
The realistic graphical interface design will be reviewed and refined as needed, including specifying the 
best methods to present clearly understandable model results.  Local plant terminology will be used in 
SimuWorks menus to make operation of the tool as familiar as possible. 
Task 5: Scoping and Design of Desired Simulation Scenarios  
The SimuWorks™ platform allows for interactive lessons to be programmed directly into the interface.  
These lessons can take the form of a series of work-at-your-own pace questions, where users are 
presented with a series of tasks to complete using the simulator.  All answers are recorded and available 
for export.  This feature is an excellent tool for creating an interactive training simulator, with plant-
specific scenarios and questions for each model. 
Hydromantis will confer with San Mateo staff to select a series of simulation scenarios that will be of 
most value to users of the model.  The scenarios may involve changes to any of the above loading, 
operational or environmental parameters.  Each scenario (including the base or “Default” scenario) will 
be defined by a series of parameter settings, including potentially reading in a time-series of input data 
109 of 312

--- page 110 ---
5 
for a dynamic simulation.  The final model deliverable will include all scenarios clearly labelled and 
defined for future use. 
Task 6: Configuration of SimuWorks 
Once the overall design is approved, Hydromantis will implement the new, graphical interface for the 
existing, calibrated plant model using the Hydromantis SimuWorks™ technology.  This will include the 
following steps: 
• 
Designing a realistic graphical representation of the plant, usually an overhead view. 
• 
Setting up inputs that are intuitive and easy to understand and access.  This can include 
interactive menus, clickable unit processes on the plant graphical view, simple methods for 
taking units out of service, and simple pop-up actions that provide help when needed. 
• 
Setting up outputs that clearly and intuitively show plant performance, including key process 
parameters like MLSS, SRT, energy usage, chemical cost and effluent quality. 
This task may require a few iterations as feedback during the design and testing will be used to refine 
the tools and features of the system. 
Task 7: Configuration of Desired Simulation Scenarios in SimuWorks 
The set of pre-defined simulation scenarios established in Task 5 will be configured in SimuWorks.   The 
scenarios will be implemented in the graphical interface via a simple, easy-to-access method, such as a 
drop-down menu, or clickable selection. 
As with the overall design of the interface, it is likely that the operational scenarios will require a few 
iterations of refinement to include all relevant feedback from the model users.  Hydromantis will engage 
with the SimuWorks users to assure that the system works as needed. 
Task 8: Documentation (Manuals) 
A set of user manuals will be created for the SimuWorks simulator.  These documents will clearly outline 
how to activate, navigate and extract information from the modelling system.  The manuals will contain 
detailed information on all aspects of the user interface, the underlying model, and the interface 
features. 
All pre-defined user scenarios will be described in the report, including how to access and utilize them 
for various modelling tasks. 
Task 9: SimuWorks Delivery and Configuration/Testing 
Once the SimuWorks simulator is completed, Hydromantis will deliver the final product to San Mateo for 
licensing and installation.  Hydromantis will be ready to assist and troubleshoot any issues encountered 
during the software installation and testing phase. 
110 of 312

--- page 111 ---
6 
Task 10: On-line Training for SimuWorks 
Hydromantis will provide on-line training for San Mateo staff in the use of the SimuWorks.  An on-line 
training session (using GoToMeeting) will be carried out to familiarize San Mateo operations staff with 
the software.  Hydromantis will create a series of exercises to go through the process of running 
simulations of the plant.  At the end of the training session(s), San Mateo staff will be able to: 
• 
navigate the SimuWorks modelling software 
• 
make changes to the model input 
• 
run simulations 
• 
observe and export simulation results 
• 
access the pre-defined simulation scenarios 
As San Mateo staff become comfortable working with the plant model, Hydromantis will collect 
feedback regarding refinements and updates to the model input, calibration, and any other changes that 
need to be made to make the model as useful as possible. 
Task 11: Software Maintenance and Support 
Hydromantis will provide 12 months of technical support and software maintenance.  This will include 
support for the following items: 
1) Software support – assistance with installation, migration and upgrades 
2) Providing upgrades and patches to the software as needed 
3) Answering questions about the software installation or usage 
4) Troubleshooting issues as requested 
5) Providing answers and advice by phone, internet teleconference, or email (9am-5pm EST) 
Task 12: 90-day Warranty 
During the 90 days following the successful installation of the modelling system, Hydromantis will 
provide full warrantied coverage to San Mateo for all corrections, updates, refinements and 
troubleshooting solutions to the modelling software.

Budget 
The required budget for the project is divided into two parts. Part 1 refers to the budget for professional 
services to develop the wastewater simulator for the San Mateo Wastewater Treatment Plant. Part 2 
refers to the cost of software licensing, training, software maintenance and support that will be required 
after completion of the project. The details of the activities/items and required budget for both Part 1 
and Part 2 is provided in tables below.  
A budget of $33,880 USD is estimated for the labor cost for development of the simulator (Part 1). 
Hydromantis will invoice the work in two installments. The first invoice of 40% will be made after the 
development of the calibrated model in GPS-X (completion of tasks 1-7). The second invoice of 60% will 
be made at the delivery of the project.  
Part 2 shows the details of the licensing and training costs.  The estimated cost for 1-day on-line training 
is $4,500 USD, and the year software license and maintenance cost for 5 licenses is $2,500 USD for the 
first year. The total budget required for Part 2 is payable upon the delivery of the completed model.  The 
software license is renewed annually.

SimuWorks will operate as standalone software applications, and therefore do not have specific system 
requirements.  The following minimum specifications are recommended for any computer running 
either modelling application: 
• 
Microsoft Windows 7 or 8 (32/64 bit) 
• 
License Server (Windows Server 2008, 2012) (only required if network licensing is being used) 
• 
3.0 GHz PC 
• 
8 Gb RAM 
• 
500 Mb Hard Disk Space 
Licensing the software via a networked license server is the preferred option, but in the event that that 
is not convenient/possible, standalone license keys can be issued instead. 
The following sections describe the features, advantages and value of the SimuWorks™ package in 
detail. 
 
 
115 of 312

--- page 116 ---
11 
SimuWorks™ - an Industry First, and Only Available from Hydromantis 
SimuWorks™ in an industry first; a flight-simulator for water and Sewage Treatment Plants.  
SimuWorks™ represents an evolution in the use of water and wastewater treatment simulation and 
modelling technology, extending its use beyond the engineering offices.  SimuWorks™ uses plant-
specific, realistic graphical interfaces to drive mathematical models built in GPS-X.  The graphics can look 
like simple schematics, realistic plant overhead views, or even replicate existing treatment plant 
supervisory control and data acquisition (SCADA) systems.  SimuWorks can provide operators with a life-
like training experience with plant response and behavior driven by sophisticated mathematical models 
of their actual plant. 
 
SimuWorks as a Training Tool 
The SimuWorks modelling environment has several power features that make it an excellent automated 
operator training system: 
1) The powerful numerical model in the background has all the predictive capabilities of the most 
sophisticated wastewater models in GPS-X, but without the complexity of the GPS-X software 
2) The realistic graphical interface provides a way for non-experts to easily access and interact with 
the model without having to conquer a steep software learning curve. 
3) Only the most common operational parameters that operators would regularly use are available 
to be adjusted, such as RAS rate, D.O. setpoint and wastage rate. 
4) Model output is configured in a graphically oriented very intuitive way.  Concentrations and 
flows are shown directly on the overhead view of the plant. 
5) Preconfigured simulation scenarios can be built directly into the model interface for easy access.  
For example, users could simply select the “Winter” scenario, and SimuWorks will automatically 
116 of 312

--- page 117 ---
12 
adjust the influent concentrations, flow rate, liquid temperature and aeration settings to typical 
winter settings. 
6) SimuWorks has a built-in “Quiz” functionality, where pre-programmed lessons are available to 
take the user through a sequence of simulations and challenges.  For example, the simulator can 
start with a plant that is not operating well, and through an automated series of simulations, 
slides and animations, show the user how to adjust the plant performance.  Users can be given 
“challenges” (e.g. take actions to reduce effluent ammonia and meet required limit) and then 
run simulations and try out ideas to achieve that goal.  This is a unique feature not found in any 
other simulation package. 
The combination of a powerful predictive model, an intuitive interface, and pre-programmed lessons 
and quizzes make SimuWorks™ uniquely the best option to deliver San Mateo SimuWorks.

Company Information 
Company Profile and Qualifications 
Hydromantis traces its roots back over 30 years as the global pioneer in the development of water and 
wastewater simulation technology.  We operate from our offices in Hamilton, Ontario, Canada with 10 
staff and our team of engineers and industry experts offer specialized professional services for 
treatment plant modelling, design and optimization to clients throughout the world.  Our technology 
sets the industry standard and we leverage the value of our broad, hands-on experience with our world 
class modelling tools to offer inventive yet realistic solutions. 
 
Hydromantis Environmental Software Solutions, Inc. is the global leader in water and wastewater 
treatment simulation software and the developer and owner of several of the most  popular software 
solutions within the industry including  GPS-X™, Toxchem™, CapdetWorks™, SimuWorks™ and WatPro™.   
We offer our customers a unique blend of consulting engineering, software, and technology transfer 
services to provide quality solutions that are cost-effective and innovative. 
 
Hydromantis provides strategic and tactical professional services.  Our domain expertise is in 
wastewater modelling which adds value in plant designing, troubleshooting and optimization for energy 
reduction and performance excellence. Our advanced process modelling capabilities can take the 
uncertainty out of critical wastewater design and operational decisions.  We are specialists in 
wastewater treatment for municipalities and industrial clients, and our engineers use their expertise in 
simulation and optimization modelling with in-depth experience and knowledge of plant operations and 
design practices. 
 
Hydromantis staff are experienced in a wide range of project activities. Our commitment is to provide 
our clients with senior engineering expertise and support.  We stay abreast of the latest developments 
in the industry, allowing us to provide our clients with the most appropriate solutions to meet their 
environmental needs. 
Company Financial Capacity and Stability 
Hydromantis is an employee-owned and managed company.  We have been in business for 30 years, 
and are continually updating and improving our unique products and services.  We are well-funded and 
well-staffed to complete the proposed project for San Mateo over the next 3 years. 
Experience Providing Similar Good and Services 
Hydromantis has been providing modelling and simulation services for public sector operations 
throughout the world for 30 years.  Hydromantis has created simulation-based tools for wastewater 
engineers for plants of all sizes, from large municipalities with centralized treatment facilities to small 
118 of 312

--- page 119 ---
14 
resort-level on-site systems.  Our library of robustly calibrated wastewater models has been developed, 
tested, calibrated and validated through three decades of service offerings. 
In the past 5 years, Hydromantis has delivered sophisticated wastewater models with operator-oriented 
graphical interfaces to over ten municipalities throughout North America.  The project that is most 
similar to the proposed project for San Mateo is the package of simulator tool that Hydromantis has 
created for the following clients: 
1) Greenville Utilities Commission, NC, USA 
2) North Davis Sewer District, UT, USA

The project for San Mateo is very similar, in that a new engineering model for the plant was created first 
(using GPS-X™), and then an operator-focused interface was applied to create an operations 
advisor/training tool (using SimuWorks™).  We have also created Sewage Treatment Plant models for 6 
treatment plants in Cincinnati, Ohio (Indian Creek, Muddy Creek, Polk Run, Sycamore Creek and Taylor 
Creek).  Cincinnati engineering and operational staff were involved throughout the project to help 
Hydromantis create an engaging and well-integrated tool for troubleshooting. 
Confidentiality of Client Information 
Hydromantis routinely receives and processes information from clients that could be considered 
confidential in nature.  For this reason, Hydromantis maintains a secure file management system within 
the Hydromantis network, which requires authentication for access.  In addition, Hydromantis 
frequently signs non-closure agreements (NDAs) with our clients regarding plant-specific information, 
performance data, and other materials.  We would be happy to sign a non-disclosure agreement with 
San Mateo as part of the project, if desired.

Subtask 2.2 –Site Visits 
The following site visits are anticipated: 
Periodic Site Visits from Design Team 
RHAA’s team will provide members of the design team to make 2 periodic site visits 
related to key design issues. The specifications call for mockup review for the 
following submittals, so reviews will need to be combined; otherwise, there will not be 
enough site visits to review submittals: 
Landscape Metalwork: 3 
Site Concrete: 2 
Precast Concrete: 2 
Planting: 1 
For each site visit, RHAA will take photographs and will prepare a site visit report that 
documents the purpose of the site visit, the outcome and results of the site visit, a 
punch list of outstanding issues or items for correction.  
Deliverables: Site visit report in PDF format with photos. 
Substantial Completion Visit 
RHAA’s team will attend a site visit at the substantial completion project milestone 
identified by the CWP and Contractor. CWP will prepare a list of items to be 
completed or corrected. RHAA’s team will review the list for concurrence.  
RHAA will take photographs and will prepare a site visit report that documents the 
purpose of the site visit, the outcome and results of the site visit, a punch list of 
outstanding issues or items for correction.

Subtask 5.1 – Technical Submittals 
RHAA will review the Contractor’s submittals, including shop drawings, as required by the 
technical specifications, for work related to RHAA’s scope of design services. RHAA will 
review and accept the Contractor’s submittals, such as shop drawings, product data, 
samples, and other data, for the limited purpose of checking for conformance with the 
design concept and the information expressed in the contract documents. This review will 
not include review of the accuracy or completeness of details, such as quantities, 
dimensions, weights or gauges, fabrication process, construction means or methods, 
coordination of the work with other trades, or construction safety precautions, all of which 
are the sole responsibility of the Contractor. Review of a specific item will not indicate that 
RHAA has reviewed the entire assembly of which the item is a component. RHAA will not be 
responsible for any deviations from the contract documents not brought to the attention of 
RHAA in writing by the Contractor. RHAA will not be required to review partial submissions 
nor those for which submissions of correlated items have not been received. 
The number of submittals was calculated based on 1.3 submittals per design drawing. Up to 
6 engineering hours are budgeted for each submittal. A 50 percent resubmission rate and 
up to 4 engineering hours per resubmittal were also assumed. Deviations from the 
anticipated schedule or duration of construction, or increased numbers of 
submittals/resubmittals will materially affect the scope of these services and RHAA’s 
compensation and will constitute additional services.  
Deliverables: 
 
Up to 96 submittals and 48 resubmittals (based on 74 drawing count). 
Subtask 5.2 – RFIs and Clarifications 
RHAA will review RFIs received from the Contractor, and will evaluate the acceptability of 
substitute materials and equipment.  
RHAA will answer questions and provide written interpretations of the requirements of the 
contract documents. Such clarifications and interpretations will be consistent with the intent 
of, and reasonably inferable from, the contract drawings and specifications.

Subtask 5.1 – Additional Technical Submittal Review (Contingency) 
If additional labor is needed to review Contractor submittals described in Subtask 5.1 of the Scope of 
Services, a budget has been established in contingency to provide 1 additional engineering hour for 
submittal review. This contingency will only be utilized if the original budget for Subtask 5.1 has been 
exhausted, and the City has provided written authorization to utilize this additional contingency 
budget for technical submittal review.  
Subtask 6.1 – Electronic O&M (eOM) Manual for GMP-3 (Contingency) 
HDR will assist the City develop an eOM manual for the Project, which will provide the City staff the 
necessary information to operate and maintain its facilities in an efficient and reliable manner. The 
eOM manual will contain useful information, that is easily accessible, organized by process area, 
including facility and equipment descriptions, design criteria, process control narratives, design 
drawings, and vendor manuals. Using the eOM manual, City staff will be able to access this 
information in an electronic format with an easy-to-use graphical user interface.  
The eOM manual will be developed as a web application and will function on a City-provided 
Microsoft Windows-based server. The eOM manual will be internally accessible and will not be 
accessible by the general public. Static data will be retrieved from SharePoint lists and libraries for 
digital presentation in the eOM manual. Equipment numbering and equipment record sheets can be 
coordinated with the City’s existing computerized maintenance management system (CMMS) to the 
greatest extent possible if requested.  
The operations manual electronic development would include the following subtasks: 
Website Map Development 
A project kick-off meeting/workshop will be held to discuss general O&M content, system 
configuration and customizations, system installation and training, coordination with the 
design team, and the overall time schedule for developing an implementation of the eOM 
manual system. A website map will be developed to illustrate the comprehensive eOM 
manual for the wastewater treatment facilities. The draft eOM Manual website map will: 
o 
Illustrate the eOM manual structure, organization, and level of detail for each unit 
process. 
o 
Explain how navigation (hyperlinks) between each section will be implemented. 
o 
Show what reference information is to be included in the eOM manual. 
The website map will be developed in coordination with CWP/City staff, and will be 
specifically tailored to meet requirements and needs of the facility staff. The site map will be 
131 of 312

--- page 132 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-2 
customized as necessary to provide the specific sub-sections desired by the plant staff. HDR 
will initially concentrate on developing the high level architecture of the eOM manual to 
define the structure and organization. HDR will prepare a draft website map for review and 
comment. HDR and City staff will then hold a four-hour workshop focused on defining the 
content format and level of detail within each unit process, including: 
o 
eOM manual guidelines and maintenance help guide. 
o 
Plant reference information. 
o 
Equipment O&M manuals provided by equipment vendors via hyperlinks to PDF files. 
o 
Unit process content details. 
The outcome of the workshop will be a defined list of content subjects the City wants in their 
eOM manual. The content definitions help describe the information available from each 
feature. Note that content definitions for this project will be specific and customized to those 
sub-sections agreed upon and defined by the website map developed with plant staff. 
The sections of the manual become the headings in the easy-to-use HTML, eOM-linked 
architecture menu system. 
Manual Content Preparation 
HDR will prepare the O&M manual content for each unit process shown in the website map. 
Example content definitions are shown in the following table. Note that content definitions for 
this project will be specific and customized to those sub-sections agreed upon and defined 
by the website map developed with plant staff. 
Example eOM Content Definitions 
Section 
Text 
Overview 
A short description of each unit process. 
Theory 
A short description of the theory behind each unit process illustrating the 
design intent. Strategies for evaluating data and making process 
adjustments. 
Figures 
Hyperlinks to 2D and 3D figures illustrating each unit process. 
Design Criteria 
Tabular listing of unit process sizes, loadings, and other design criteria. 
Components 
Hyperlinks to equipment manuals provided by equipment vendors as PDF 
files.  
Controls 
A description of manual and automatic controls.  
System 
Procedures 
A list of duties to be performed by operators when making daily process 
checks. General procedures for starting up and shutting down the process. 
Troubleshooting 
A list of process alarms showing possible causes and suggested responses. 
Safety 
General safety considerations for the unit process.

--- page 133 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-3 
Existing equipment O&M manuals that are only available in hard copy may be scanned into 
PDF files and hyperlinked within the eOM manual, but will not be included in this scope of 
services initially. City personnel will be trained on procedures for completing this effort 
following project completion. Equipment record sheets will be stored as PDF files.  
If requested, the City’s existing facilities can be incorporated into an existing comprehensive 
resource for the operators (not included in budget at this time). Active links provide 
comprehensive groups of information that reference other relevant documents stored in the 
eOM database. 
Graphic Content Definition 
HDR will develop 3D figures for communicating to plant O&M staff the design intent, and how 
to operate the unit process. The figures will be developed from the conformed contract 
drawings, but will be modified by deleting extraneous construction-related information that is 
not pertinent to O&M personnel. The figures will be prepared in AutoCAD, Visio, and/or 
PowerPoint, and converted to PDF files for inclusion in the eOM manual. The graphics will 
be sized for the monitor size the City intends to use to access the eOM manual. Up to 40 2D 
and 20 3D figures are anticipated. In addition, HDR will incorporate the plant as-built 
drawings into the eOM manual as PDF files, and provide hyperlinks to each group of 
drawings. 
System Configuration and Customization 
HDR will develop specific system customizations, including screen layouts, file formats, 
administration, and integration needs. Technology issues related to installation on a City web 
server will be identified. 
System Installation 
HDR will develop the draft and final eOM manuals on an HDR server. The draft and final 
versions will be available to CWP/City staff via the Internet for review. HDR will coordinate 
installation of the final eOM manual on the City’s server with the City's information 
technology (IT) staff at the end of the project. The final eOM Manual will be downloaded to 
the City’s network server via an HDR FTP site. 
System Training 
HDR will schedule a meeting with the plant staff, and facilitate two 4-hour training sessions 
for the plant staff on how to use and maintain the eOM manual. The training sessions will 
provide general instruction and use of the eOM manual, and will provide instruction on how 
the plant staff can edit and revise the eOM manual. Training will also be provided to the 
City's IT staff on eOM manual system administration, maintenance, and security. One 4-hour 
training session has been budgeted for this effort. The computers and servers necessary to 
view the eOM manual are not included with the production of the eOM manual.  
The following lists the City requirements for the eOM manual. 
 
Provide necessary software on the City’s computers to enable the eOM manual to function. 
The eOM manual hardware and software will be supplied by the City, and will meet the 
minimum requirements as follows:

 
Draft eOM manual in electronic format accessible by plant staff via the Internet. 
 
Final eOM manual in electronic format downloadable to the City network server via an HDR 
FTP site. 
 
Memoranda and meeting notes, as required. 
Subtask 6.3 - Training Assistance for GMP-3 (Contingency) 
HDR will assist the CWP, Contractor, and City in O&M training for new unit processes and auxiliary 
systems, while the City’s operations staff prepares to operate the new unit processes during startup.  
Early in the construction phase of the project, HDR will provide a template to CWP and the 
Contractor for a detailed written training plan. This document will include the details of the training of 
City employees on the new equipment and processes. CWP and the Contractor will develop the 
135 of 312

--- page 136 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-6 
section on vendor equipment training, while HDR will develop the section process training. HDR will 
review and comment on this document, and ultimately approve the official version. This will be a 
living document and will require frequent updating as dates changes due to shifting construction 
schedules.  
HDR will provide training to operations staff on each of the process areas of the project. These 
trainings will go beyond the equipment-specific training provided by the equipment vendors. Each 
training will cover process operation, process goals, design loadings, process control, and 
adjustments. Training will be in the form of formal classroom, site “show and tell” presentations, and 
shift change presence to answer questions and make sure operating characteristics of new 
processes are accurately conveyed and understood by every operator. This instruction shall cover 
both the basic operational concept and actual operation of the systems and components under both 
normal and abnormal operations that are likely to occur. 
These trainings will be repeated as necessary to cover operator shifts and may be recorded by the 
City to use for new employee training purposes. 
The trainers will be identified in the training plan, but will be a combination of project engineers and 
startup team members that are familiar with the project. 
Although training for the Hydromantis Simulator will be included in the training plan, its associated 
cost is captured in Subtask 6.4. 
B&C has budgeted for up to 120 hours to provide assistance to HDR, the CWP, Contractor, and City 
in O&M training for new I&C systems. This will include reviewing and providing input to HDR’s 
training presentations as it relates to I&C systems. This work will be performed at the request of 
HDR up to the limit of the budget. Two overnight site visits are included in the task budget. It is 
assumed that all training activities that require B&C’s input will take place during daytime work 
hours.  
Expense assumptions for the training assistance are as follows: 
 
Per diem per day for lodging, meals, and Incidentals, complying with GSA rates for San 
Mateo, California ($325/day is assumed in Attachment A-2). 
 
Mileage from Reno, Nevada, complying with GSA rates for San Mateo, California ($300 per 
trip is assumed in Attachment A-2). 
 
$1,200 estimated total cost per trip for airfare, rental car, and gas for team members 
traveling to/from Irvine, California. 
 
$1,500 estimated total cost per trip for airfare, rental car, and gas for team members travling 
to/from Portland, Oregon or Phoenix, Arizona, complying with GSA rates for San Mateo, 
California. 
Deliverables: Training workshop materials and handouts. 
Subtask 6.4 – Treatment Plant Simulator (Contingency) 
HDR’s subconsultant, Hydromantis, will provide wastewater treatment process simulator for the 
City’s wastewater treatment system so that the model can be used to troubleshoot plant upsets and 
136 of 312

--- page 137 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-7 
impact to effluent quality, support plant process optimization efforts and disaster recovery plans, and 
provide automated training to new operational staff.  
The mathematical model that was created in 2018 for the biological, chemical, and physical 
treatment sections of the wastewater treatment plant will be updated to incorporate the new wet 
weather operating mode. The mathematical model will be configured in the SimuWorks graphical 
interface, to be used by the City’s operational staff, for day-to-day operational and troubleshooting 
advice, and for operator training. The model will have plant-specific, realistic graphical 
representations of the actual wastewater treatment system being simulated. The model inputs will be 
restricted to typical operational parameters that operators would adjust at the real plant. 
Hydromantis will work together with HDR and the City’s project manager to assist in testing, 
troubleshooting, and resolving issues. Hydromantis will provide support installation support and 
online training for engineering and operations staff members in the use of the model. Hydromantis 
will conduct training sessions to train City staff regarding the use of the model. The goal of the 
training is to “train the trainers” so that City staff members can train others within the organization as 
needed. 
Hydromantis will provide software license for the maximum of 5 concurrent users. Licenses delivered 
will be annual, renewable licenses. 
The following subtasks are anticipated: 
Task 6.4.1 - Project Management 
In this activity, regular communication through email and phone will be performed to 
coordinate activities and manage resources for timely completion of the project. Regular 
progress meeting will be held to discuss the progress of the project and identify critical items 
needing attention. 
Task 6.4.2 - Kick-off Meeting 
The project will start with a kick-off meeting with HDR and San Mateo staff to discuss the 
scope and details of the project. The focus of the kick-off meeting will be for Hydromantis to 
review the updated wet weather operation and to jointly discuss a set of simulation scenarios 
to be developed for the calibrated model. Details about how the modelling software will 
ultimately deployed and licensed will also be discussed. 
Task 6.4.3 - Update Model Wet Weather Operation 
Hydromantis will take the San Mateo GPS-X™ model originally created in 2018 and update 
the dry/wet weather operational models. The custom code for setting flow splitting, bypass 
pumping, clarifier operation, activated sludge tank operation, and other flow control will be 
modified to match to the new approach. Other modifications to the GPS-X™ model required 
to support the new operation will be made at this time.  
Once built and calibrated, the model can be used to predict the effects of the biological 
growth processes and solids separation on conventional water quality parameters including 
cBOD5, COD, TKN, TSS, total NH3-N, NO2-N, NO3-N, total phosphorus, soluble phosphorus, 
pH/Alkalinity. The level of detail in the model will be equivalent or more than the International 
Water Association (IWA) family of activated sludge models (such as ASM1, ASM2d, ASM3, 
137 of 312

--- page 138 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-8 
etc., which are all included in GPS-X™). Model selection for the various plant processes will 
be based on consultations between Hydromantis, HDR, and City staff. 
The process model will be able to execute both steady state and dynamic simulations and 
respond to changes to the input variables. The process model will be predominantly 
mechanistic and can predict the performance of each individual process based on 
engineering principles. For normal plant operation, the model can predict the effect of varying 
input or control variables such as chemical dosages, oxygen feed rates, increases in 
average daily flow, RAS and WAS flow rates, MLSS and/or SRT, wastewater temperature, 
influent quality, recycle ratio, accepting varying amounts of supernatant and septic waste and 
varying quality of raw sewage. 
Task 6.4.4 - Scoping and Design of SimuWorks Interface 
Once the underlying GPS-X model has been finalized, Hydromantis with meet with HDR and 
City staff to scope out and design the SimuWorks interface. Hydromantis will engage staff in 
scoping exercises designed to determine the most appropriate forms of model inputs and 
controls to be used. The realistic graphical interface design will be reviewed and refined as 
needed, including specifying the best methods to present clearly understandable model 
results. Local plant terminology will be used in SimuWorks menus to make operation of the 
tool as familiar as possible. 
Task 6.4.5 - Scoping and Design of Desired Simulation Scenarios 
The SimuWorks™ platform allows for interactive lessons to be programmed directly into the 
interface. These lessons can take the form of a series of work-at-your-own pace questions, 
where users are presented with a series of tasks to complete using the simulator. Answers 
are recorded and available for export. This feature is an excellent tool for creating an 
interactive training simulator, with plant-specific scenarios and questions for each model. 
Hydromantis will confer with City staff to select a series of simulation scenarios that will be of 
most value to users of the model. The scenarios may involve changes to any of the above 
loading, operational or environmental parameters. Each scenario (including the base or 
“Default” scenario) will be defined by a series of parameter settings, including potentially 
reading in a time-series of input data for a dynamic simulation. The final model deliverable 
will include all scenarios clearly labelled and defined for future use. 
Task 6.4.6 - Configuration of SimuWorks 
Once the overall design is approved, Hydromantis will implement the new, graphical 
interface for the existing, calibrated plant model using the Hydromantis SimuWorks™ 
technology. This will include the following steps: 
o 
Designing a realistic graphical representation of the plant, usually an overhead view. 
o 
Setting up inputs that are intuitive and easy to understand and access. This can include 
interactive menus, clickable unit processes on the plant graphical view, simple methods 
for taking units out of service, and simple pop-up actions that provide help when needed. 
o 
Setting up outputs that clearly and intuitively show plant performance, including key 
process parameters like MLSS, SRT, energy usage, chemical cost and effluent quality.  
138 of 312

--- page 139 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-9 
This task may require a few iterations as feedback during the design and testing will be used 
to refine the tools and features of the system. 
Task 6.4.7 - Configuration of Desired Simulation Scenarios in SimuWorks 
The set of pre-defined simulation scenarios established in Task 6.4.5 will be configured in 
SimuWorks. The scenarios will be implemented in the graphical interface via a simple, easy-
to-access method, such as a drop-down menu, or clickable selection. 
As with the overall design of the interface, it is likely that the operational scenarios will 
require a few iterations of refinement to include all relevant feedback from the model users. 
Hydromantis will engage with the SimuWorks users to assure that the system works as 
needed. 
Task 6.4.8 - Documentation (Manuals) 
A set of user manuals will be created for the SimuWorks simulator. These documents will 
clearly outline how to activate, navigate and extract information from the modelling system. 
The manuals will contain detailed information on all aspects of the user interface, the 
underlying model, and the interface features. 
Pre-defined user scenarios will be described in the report, including how to access and utilize 
them for various modelling tasks. 
Task 6.4.9 - SimuWorks Delivery and Configuration/Testing 
Once the SimuWorks simulator is completed, Hydromantis will deliver the final product to the 
City for licensing and installation. Hydromantis will be ready to assist and troubleshoot issues 
encountered during the software installation and testing phase. 
Task 6.4.10: Online Training for SimuWorks 
Hydromantis will provide online training for San Mateo staff in the use of the SimuWorks. An 
online training session (using GoToMeeting) will be carried out to familiarize City operations 
staff with the software. Hydromantis will create a series of exercises to go through the 
process of running simulations of the plant. At the end of the training session(s), City staff will 
be able to: 
o 
Navigate the SimuWorks modelling software 
o 
Make changes to the model input 
o 
Run simulations 
o 
Observe and export simulation results 
o 
Access the pre-defined simulation scenarios 
As City staff become comfortable working with the plant model, Hydromantis will collect 
feedback regarding refinements and updates to the model input, calibration, and other 
changes that need to be made to make the model as useful as possible. 
139 of 312

--- page 140 ---
20-10075318 
10/9/20 
Page A-3-10 
Task 6.4.11 - Software Maintenance and Support 
Hydromantis will provide 12 months of technical support and software maintenance. This will 
include support for the following items: 
o 
Software support – assistance with installation, migration and upgrades 
o 
Providing upgrades and patches to the software, as needed 
o 
Answering questions about the software installation or usage 
o 
Troubleshooting issues as requested 
o 
Providing answers and advice by phone, internet teleconference, or email (9am-5pm 
EST) 
Task 6.4.12 - 90-day Warranty 
During the 90 days following the successful installation of the modelling system, Hydromantis 
will provide full warrantied coverage to the City for corrections, updates, refinements and 
troubleshooting solutions to the modelling software. 
Task 7 – Resident Engineer for 2022 
Subtask 7.3 – Resident Engineer for 2022 
HDR may provide an onsite resident engineer during major construction activity of the new 
wastewater treatment plant facilities in GMP-3, from January 1, 2022 through December 31, 2022, to 
facilitate efficient Contractor submittal and RFI coordination with HDR’s design resources, as well as 
other communications among HDR designers, CWP, Contractor, and the City.  
HDR’s resident engineer will attend weekly construction progress meetings with the CWP, 
Contractor, and the City. The resident engineer will also attend other meetings that may be required 
to review issues. 
Labor and Expense assumptions for the Resident Engineer are as follows: 
 
Budgeted labor for 2022 is 1,968 hours (249 work days) 
 
Expense budget for 2022 assumes daily mileage to and from Walnut Creek, CA for 50% of 
the year or, $64 per day; and weekly mileage to and from Folsom, CA, approximately $155 
per week, and daily lodging and meals, approximately $315 per day for 50% of the year, all 
complying with GSA rates for San Mateo, California.

MEETING DATE:
November 02, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant Immediate Action Projects, Package III – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 1 of the professional services agreement to HDR, Inc. to provide engineering services for 
Immediate Action Projects, Package III in an amount not to exceed $801,564;  increase the contingency reserve in an 
amount not to exceed $60,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement and issue change 
orders within the contingency amount in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The wastewater treatment plant (WWTP) is an aging facility, and the Clean Water Program (CWP) includes a variety of 
capital improvement projects to rehabilitate and upgrade the existing facilities. Immediate Action Projects, Package III (IAP 
III) includes improvements to the WWTP’s effluent pump station, site waste pump station, and plant-wide mechanical and 
electrical equipment. IAP III was planned to be executed in three phases: Phase 1 - Project Analyses, Phase 2 – Detailed 
Design and Bid Phase Services, and Phase 3 - Construction Services. 
On September 16, 2019, City Council awarded the professional services agreement to HDR to proceed with Phase 1 
activities. Phase 1 was completed, and the analysis performed has been incorporated into the scope of this amendment to 
proceed with Phase 2 – Detailed Design. A future amendment for Phase 3 – Engineering Services During Construction is 
anticipated and the fee will be negotiated upon the completion of Phase 2. Finalization of this fee will be negotiated at the 
completion of Phase 2 and will be added to the contract by amendment with City Council approval.   
BUDGET IMPACT:
The IAP III project is funded by the WWTP Immediate Action Projects Package III project, which has sufficient funding for 
Amendment No. 1.

20-10184901 
1
City of San Mateo Clean Water Program 
Immediate Action Projects, Package III (Job No. 46T010) 
Phase 2  Detailed Design 
The following scope of work involves providing preliminary design, detailed design, and bidding 
services for the City/CWP of San Mateo (City/CWP) Clean Water Program (CWP) Immediate Action 
Projects, Package III (Job No. 46T010), located at the San Mateo/Estero Municipal Improvement 
District (EMID) Wastewater Treatment Plant.  
PROJECT DESCRIPTION 
HDR prepared a Project Analysis Report (Phase 1) for the Immediate Action Projects, Package III. 
Based on the recommendations of the report, the following items will be included in the scope of 
services: 
EFFLUENT PUMPING STATION (EPS) IMPROVEMENTS 
Add one new 20 mgd EPS 2 pump and associated piping, fittings, and valves. 
Rebuild three existing pumps, motors, and isolation valves at EPS 2. Evaluate and mitigate the 
effects of new variable frequency drives (VFDs) with the existing motors. 
Replace doors and windows in the EPS. Correct roof leak and paint the interior and exterior
pump station. 
Provide structural modifications to include replacing existing concrete overhangs, providing a 
new floor penetration for the new pump, and providing concrete repairs as needed. 
Add four new VFDs and anti-ratcheting devices for the existing and proposed EPS 2 pumps 
located in the EPS1 building. New motor control center (MCC) 900N and MCC-900E that feed 
the EPS and consolidate existing plant loads that will remain in service after the Nutrient 
Removal and Wet Weather Upgrades project.  
Provide non-structural improvements to EPS 2 pump suction cans and EPS 1 pump bays by 
adding baffles or intake screens, to improve hydraulics. It is assumed that the improvements will 
be designed so that new components are installed directly inside the cans or wetwell or attach 
components to the pump columns or pumps. 
Provide miscellaneous electrical, instrumentation, control, and programming improvements.
1
155 of 312

--- page 156 ---
20-10184901 
2
Develop new pump control narrative for the combined EPS1 and EPS2 operation. Evaluate the 
use of existing gravity flow option and determine equipment and re-programming required to flow 
by gravity to the bay when required. Actual reprogramming is not part of scope. The City shall 
test existing system for gravity flow conditions and at low to high tide conditions. 
Replace three existing check valves with new check valves of the same type at EPS 1. 
Assumption: No replacement of the existing flow meters upstream of EPS 1 and EPS 2. 
SITE WASTE PUMPING STATION (SWPS): 
Review recommended SWPS location from the IAPIII Project Analysis Report with the City to 
confirm feasibility. Evaluate up to one additional location for new SWPS prior to design of 
pumping station if required. 
Provide new concrete wet well and valve vault for pump discharge piping, valves, and flowmeter 
per Hydraulic Institute (HI) standards. The new wet well and valve vault structure will be buried 
with a deep foundation system.  
Provide three submersible chopper pumps, and associated piping, valves, and fittings. 
Coordinate with pump manufacturers for final selection and sizing. 
Design necessary civil and yard piping improvements to route site waste flow from the Solids 
Handling Building to the new pumping station.  
Provide new citric acid tank, feed pumps and piping for chemical dose to new pumping station 
location. 
Provide piping modifications within the existing Solids Handling Building basement to convey 
building process and drain flow to the new pump station. 
Provide VFDs for the submersible pumps, and other electrical, instrumentation, control, and 
programming improvements for the new pumping station. 
Pump control narratives for the new pumping station. 
PLANT-WIDE MECHANICAL IMPROVEMENTS: 
Provide new split air conditioning systems with condensing units and air handling units at the 
EPS electrical room and pump room. 
Replace current louver and add filter housing at the louver in main structure. 
Provide new split heat pump system with heat pump unit and air handling unit at the solids 
building control room. Replace existing filters on the electrical room supply fan. 
Provide new split air-conditioning system with a condensing unit and an air handling unit for the 
digester control building electrical room. 
156 of 312

--- page 157 ---
20-10184901 
3
PLANT-WIDE ELECTRICAL IMPROVEMENTS: 
Design two new MCCs to replace MCCs P1, P2, P3, and P4. 
Provide a summary of existing and future electrical demands. 
SCOPE OF WORK 
HDR will provide detailed design and bidding services for the recommended improvements 
described above.  
TASK 1 - PROJECT MANAGEMENT AND COORDINATION 
This task covers general project management, meetings, quality control, and coordination activities 
through the following tasks and through Task 4  Bidding Services.  
Task 1.1  Project Management 
Task 1.1.1  General Management 
HDR will manage the project, including subconsultants, to adhere to the scope, budget, and 
schedule, and will keep the CWP/City appraised of the status of the project.  
A project management plan (PMP) will be developed as a communication tool to the City/CWP, 
CWP, and HDR team (including subconsultants). The PMP will include project development plan, a 
project schedule, project team contact list, quality management plan, change management plan, 
communication plan, risk register and management plan, health and safety plan, and project 
administration requirements. A draft PMP will be issued to the City/CWP for comments. Comments 
will be addressed in a final PMP. 
Other activities under this task include project set-up, document management, administration, and 
staff management. 
Deliverables: Draft and final PMP in PDF format. 
Task 1.1.2  Progress Reports 
HDR will prepare and submit monthly progress reports that include a summary of the work 
completed by task, project action item log, upcoming work, project issues, budget and schedule 
status, percent complete, cost to complete, earned value versus actual spent analysis, potential 
scope or budget changes, and other important project information. The monthly progress report will 
be submitted with the project invoice as part of the monthly request for payment.  
Deliverables: Monthly progress reports in PDF format. 
Task 1.1.3  Project Invoices 
HDR 
will document the man-hours and billing rates for staff for each task in the work breakdown structure 
(WBS), as well as overhead, profit, and direct costs. The current and previous billing period 
invoicing, as well as a summary of the budget spent, budget remaining, cost to complete, and 
backup documentation for expenses will be included. The monthly progress report and project 
schedule will be submitted with the project invoice as part of the monthly request for payment. 
157 of 312

--- page 158 ---
20-10184901 
4
Deliverables: Monthly invoices in PDF format. 
Task 1.1.4  Progress Schedule 
HDR will create a baseline project schedule with tasks and task durations, and submit it for the 
City/CWP
-loaded to calculate a monthly earned value of work 
performed. HDR will prepare a planned value curve at the beginning of the project. 
HDR will prepare and deliver a project schedule each month in PDF format using P6. HDR will 
provide the percent complete for each activity worked on during the billing period and calculate the 
earned value for the month. The earned value will be compared to the planned value and the actual 
invoice value for the month. HDR will include justification for requests for monies over the planned 
value, and explain how the overall budget will be met over the life of the project. Each month 
schedule update will include a four-week lookahead. 
Deliverables: Initial baseline schedule with updated NTP start date. Monthly progress schedule to 
be included with the final version of the monthly invoice and progress report 
submittal. PDF and P6 file of the monthly progress schedule. 
Task 1.2  Risk Management Assistance 
HDR will assist the City/CWP with maintenance of the City/CWP risk management plan and risk 
-off meeting with 
the City/CWP, the City/CWP risk management plan will be shared and risks will be jointly reviewed, 
new risks will be identified, and mitigation of potential risks to the project will be discussed. HDR will 
provide updates to the City/CWP risk management plan and mitigate applicable project risks
throughout the work.  
Deliverables: Risk management plan updates in PDF format. 
Task 1.3  Workshops and Meetings 
HDR will attend the following meetings: 
Two-hour kick-off virtual conference call/on-line meeting, to be attended by up to four HDR team 
members. The budget is based on one kick-off conference call/on-line meeting. A portion of the 
kick-off meeting will be devoted to discussion of the risk management plan. 
One-hour bi-weekly project progress meetings will be conducted by virtual conference calls/on-
line meetings with up to three HDR team members throughout the duration of the project. 
Progress virtual calls/on-line meetings will include a review the status of the project scope, 
schedule, budget, and a discussion of ongoing project tasks.  
One-hour design criteria virtual workshop at the start of the preliminary design to review design 
criteria with the City/CWP. Up to three HDR team members will attend the virtual workshop.
Four two-hour submittal review virtual calls/on-line meetings at the City/CWP
 for each of 
the meetings at the 30%, 60%, 90%, and 100% stages of design. The 30% deliverable review 
meeting will held virtually and the 60%, 90%, and 100% stage meeting will be help in-person. 
HDR will prepare and distribute draft agenda and meeting minutes to attendees to review and 
comment. The final meeting minutes will be distributed after addressing comments.

Task 1.6  Agency Coordination 
HDR will assist the City/CWP in coordinating the project with various local/county, state/regional, 
and federal agencies, as required. This task includes attending meetings, as needed, with applicable 
agencies, providing meeting notes, and providing project information and exhibits to the agencies. 
This task is an allowance task and will only be used when specifically requested by the City/CWP in 
writing. Costs for this task will be invoiced as a separate line item and invoicing will include a copy of 
the authorization from the City/CWP.  
Up to two agency coordination virtual calls/on-line meetings have been budgeted. Each virtual 
call/on-line meeting is assumed to be up to two hours in length, and is assumed to be attended by 
up to two HDR team members.  
TASK 2  PRELIMINARY DESIGN 
Task 2.1 - Design Criteria 
Utilizing the Alternatives Analysis TM developed in Phase 1, HDR will formulate design criteria of the 
project design elements identified above to develop the design. HDR will review the recommended 
SWPS location from the IAPIII Project Analysis Report with the City to confirm feasibility and will 
evaluate up to one additional location for new SWPS prior to design of pumping station, if required. 
HDR will lead one two-hour virtual workshop to review the design criteria with the City/CWP, to be 
attended by up to three HDR team members (budgeted under Task 1.3). HDR will incorporate 
City/CWP comments into a final design criteria document. COVID-19 social distancing and facial 
mask protocols will be followed for in-person site visits, if still applicable.

Assumptions: 
A new geotechnical report, survey, or potholing efforts are not included under the scope of work. 
The existing information completed for the WWTP under the Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather 
Upgrades Project will be utilized for this project. 
Figures will be created in Bluebeam or Adobe format. 
Deliverables: Draft and final PDF of technical memo in PDF format. 
Task 2.2  Field Investigations 
HDR will conduct field investigations to verify conflicts, confirm dimensions, confirm as-built 
information, and take photos for demo drawings.  
Assumptions: 
Two site visits with attendance of up to three HDR team members will be scheduled. 
COVID-19 social distancing and facial mask protocols will be followed for in-person site visits, if 
still applicable. 
Deliverables: None. 
Task 2.3  30% Design Development 
The design activities and design elements will be developed to a 30% level of completion. This will 
include preliminary design of all project elements defined under the project description and will 
include alternatives evaluation for major equipment selection and design criteria for new equipment 
and upgrades. The 30% design level will include a development of AACE Class 3 construction cost 
estimate and preliminary construction sequencing plan and schedule. The 30% design level plans
will be developed and will include major process drawings, site plan, process flow diagram and 
process and instrumentation diagrams (P&IDs). HDR will lead one two-hour virtual workshop
(budgeted under Task 1.3) to present the deliverable in preparation for City/CWP review and one 
two-hour workshop (budgeted under Task 1.3) to present responses to City/CWP review comments 
to freeze the design definition, to be attended by up to three HDR team members.  
Deliverables: Workshop/meeting agendas and notes in PDF format. Other deliverables included 
under Task 2.4 
Task 2.4  Basis of Design Report (BODR) 
HDR will update the Alternatives Analysis TM developed in Phase 1 to a Basis of Design Report 
(BODR). The BODR that will summarize the elements discussed under Task 2.3 into the BODR. 
Deliverables: Draft and Final PDF of BODR in PDF format. BODR will include the following 
BODR updates in PDF format that includes: 
o

TASK 3  FINAL DESIGN 
HDR will prepare 60%, 90%, and 100% design packages for the selected project alternatives. The 
BODR will be updated with any major new decisions at the 60% submittal.

Task 3.1  60% Design Development 
The design shall be updated to a 60% level of completion. HDR will incorporate applicable review 
comments from the 30% design phase. Discipline calculations, updated AACE Class 2 construction 
cost estimate with basis of estimate narrative, construction sequencing plan and schedule, and 60%
design level plans will be included to reflect the status of the drawings and will support the 60% 
design submittal workshops. City/CWP comments provided on the previous submittal will be 
resolved, rejected, addressed, and/or incorporated in this submittal. HDR will lead up to one two-
hour design review workshop at the project site after delivery of the 60% design submittal (budgeted 
under Task 1.3) and one two-hour workshop (budgeted under Task 1.3) to present responses to 
City/CWP review comments from the 30% design phase. Each workshop or meeting will be attended 
by up to three HDR team members.  
Deliverables: 
60% Design drawings in PDF format. 
Major equipment specifications in PDF format. 
Discipline calculations, updated AACE Class 2 construction cost estimate, and updated 
construction sequencing plan and schedule in PDF format. 
Workshop/meeting agendas and notes in PDF format. 
City/CWP/HDR comment form with review comments and adjudications. (Implementation of 
comments to be made at the 90% design phase). 
Task 3.2  90% Design 
The design shall be updated to a 90% level of completion. HDR will incorporate applicable review 
comments from the 60% design phase. Discipline calculations, updated AACE Class 1 construction 
cost estimate with basis of estimate narrative, construction sequencing plan and schedule, and 90%
design level plans will be included to reflect the status of the drawings and will support the 90% 
design submittal workshops. Supplementary/auxiliary design elements will be incorporated between 
the 60% and 90% design submittals. Drawings for all disciplines shall be substantially complete. 
Specifications shall be substantially complete and include complete sections and divisions, including 
,
and complete plans and specifications. No new drawings and/or specification sections shall be 
provided after this stage.

The final check set shall include all bid documents. HDR will perform a final inter-disciplinary cross-
check of the design changes made since the 90% design submittal and will correct the related 
discrepancies. 
No new drawings or changes to the plans or specifications will be provided that are not a result of 
comments received by the City/CWP, regulatory review, or a final in-house quality control check. 
HDR and the City/CWP shall conduct an up to two-hour virtual workshop (budgeted under Task 1.3) 
to verify that all City/CWP comments have been addressed and all permit conditions are accounted 
for. After the City/CWP
-check review is complete, HDR will revise the documents and submit 
Final Bid Documents. The Final Bid Documents will include finished, checked, and completed plans 
and specifications, and will incorporate all City/CWP comments from previous submittals, 
workshops, and constructability reviews as appropriate.  
HDR will document in-house changes and submit them to the City/CWP along with the Final Bid 
Documents. The Final Design submittals will also include updated preliminary design report, updated 
AACE Class 1 construction cost estimate with basis of estimate narrative, construction sequencing 
plan and schedule, and final project quality control documentation. Plans, detailed specifications,

City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
November 02, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant Centrifuges Repair – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing process for the  agreement with GEA Mechanical Equipment US 
Inc. for the wastewater treatment plant centrifuges repair in the amount of $162,200 and authorize the Public Works 
Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
Two of the wastewater treatment plant (WWTP) centrifuges have failed and require immediate major service. The 
centrifuges are vital pieces of equipment in the WWTP process. These units remove the remaining water from digested 
solids to produce a compatible material ("cake") that can then be hauled away to be used for either landfill alternate daily 
cover or land application. This is critical to maintain compliance in operations. Digested sludge could not be processed if 
these units were to fail so rental equipment is currently being used to continue the processing of sludge.
Due to the precise nature of centrifuge operation, factory-trained technicians are needed to complete these repairs. 
GEA/WESTFALIA is the original manufacturer of these units and have factory-trained technicians available locally 
(Patterson, CA) to conduct repairs, both at their facility and on-site.
Staff recommends award the agreement to GEA Mechanical Equipment US Inc. for the repair of the failed centrifuges.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The cost of the centrifuge repairs were not budgeted, but sufficient funds are available in the WWTP maintenance budget 
to fund this agreement. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This contract is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Proposed Resolution
Att 2 – Agreement
