RESOLUTION NO. ____ (20__)
APPROVING ALTERNATIVE PURCHASING PROCEDURE FOR AN AGREEMENT WITH GEA/WESTFALIA FOR THE
WASTEWATER TREATMENT PLANT CENTRIFUGES REPAIR PROJECT
WHEREAS, the Wastewater Treatment Plant Centrifuges Repair Project (the “Project”), is necessary to 
repair two failed Wastewater Treatment Plant Centrifuges; and
WHEREAS, the centrifuges are vital pieces of equipment in the WWTP process; and
WHEREAS, the precise nature of centrifuge operation requires factory-trained technicians to complete 
these repairs; and 
WHEREAS, GEA/WESTFALIA is the original manufacturer of these units and have factory-trained 
technicians available locally to conduct repairs, both at their facility and on-site; and
WHEREAS, in accordance with Municipal Code section 3.60.050 (b) agreements may be awarded without 
competitive bids if calling for bids would be impracticable, unavailing or impossible and the City Council sets 
forth findings designating the reasons; and
WHEREAS, City staff recommends approval of the agreement with GEA/Westfalia for $162,200; 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY FINDS and 
RESOLVES that:
1.
This contract is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of 
the operation, repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing 
public or private structures, facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, 
involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
2. In accordance with Municipal Code section 3.60.050 (b), calling for bids would be impracticable 
because:  
a)
GEA/WESTFALIA is the original manufacturer of these units and have factory-trained 
technicians available locally to conduct repairs, both at their facility and on-site.
3.
The agreement with GEA/Westfalia, for the Centrifuge Repair in the amount of $162,200 is 
approved.
4.
The Public Works Director is authorized to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
submitted, on behalf of the City.

Agreement. The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court,
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions. It
is the intent of this provision that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.

SECTION 17 - NON-DISCRIMINATION

CONTRACTOR warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity. Neither CONTRACTOR nor any of its
subcontractors shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.

SECTION 18 - MEDIATION

Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to
mediation. The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request. The mediator shall be
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service. The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.

The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties. Neither party shall be deemed the
prevailing party. No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement. The mediation process, once
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

SECTION 19 - LITIGATION

CONTRACTOR shall testify at CITY'S request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection
with CONTRACTOR'S services under this Agreement. Unless the action is brought by CONTRACTOR, or
is based upon CONTRACTOR'S wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONTRACTOR for preparation for
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONTRACTOR'S standard hourly rates at the time of actual
testimony.

SECTION 20 - NOTICES

All notices hereunder shall be given in writing and mailed, postage prepaid, addressed as
follows:

EXHIBIT B
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE

Coverage shall be at least as broad as:

1. Commercial General Liability (CGL): Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal &
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.

2. Automobile Liability: ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.

3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury
or disease.

If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor.

Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:

Additional Insured Status

The City of San Mateo and the Estero Municipal Improvement District, their elected and appointed
officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on the auto policy for liability arising
out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf of the Contractor; and on the
CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations performed by or on behalf of the
Contractor including materials, parts or equipment furnished in connection with such work or
operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an endorsement to the
Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 20 10 and CG 20 37
forms if later revisions used).

Primary Coverage

For any claims related to this contract, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance
as respects the City of San Mateo and the Estero Municipal Improvement District, their elected and
appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City of
San Mateo and the Estero Municipal Improvement District, their elected and appointed officials,
employees, or agents shall be excess of the Contractor’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after

thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

Waiver of Subrogation

Contractor hereby grants to the City of San Mateo and the Estero Municipal Improvement District a
waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said Contractor may acquire against the City by
virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance. Contractor agrees to obtain any endorsement
that may be necessary to effect this waiver of subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of
whether or not the City has received a waiver of subrogation endorsement from the insurer.

Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions

Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may
require the Contractor to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof of
ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within the
retention.

Acceptability of Insurers

Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless
otherwise acceptable to the City.

Verification of Coverage

Contractor shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies of
the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause. All certificates and
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences. However, failure
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the Contractor’s
obligation to provide them. The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

CONSUMER DISCLOSURE

From time to time, Carahsoft OBO City of San Mateo (we, us or Company) may be required by
law to provide to you certain written notices or disclosures. Described below are the terms and
conditions for providing to you such notices and disclosures electronically through the
DocuSign, Inc. (DocuSign) electronic signing system. Please read the information below
carefully and thoroughly, and if you can access this information electronically to your
satisfaction and agree to these terms and conditions, please confirm your agreement by clicking
the ‘I agree’ button at the bottom of this document.

Getting paper copies

At any time, you may request from us a paper copy of any record provided or made available
electronically to you by us. You will have the ability to download and print documents we send
to you through the DocuSign system during and immediately after signing session and, if you
elect to create a DocuSign signer account, you may access them for a limited period of time
(usually 30 days) after such documents are first sent to you. After such time, if you wish for us to
send you paper copies of any such documents from our office to you, you will be charged a
$0.00 per-page fee. You may request delivery of such paper copies from us by following the
procedure described below.

Withdrawing your consent

If you decide to receive notices and disclosures from us electronically, you may at any time
change your mind and tell us that thereafter you want to receive required notices and disclosures
only in paper format. How you must inform us of your decision to receive future notices and
disclosure in paper format and withdraw your consent to receive notices and disclosures
electronically is described below.

Consequences of changing your mind

If you elect to receive required notices and disclosures only in paper format, it will slow the
speed at which we can complete certain steps in transactions with you and delivering services to
you because we will need first to send the required notices or disclosures to you in paper format,
and then wait until we receive back from you your acknowledgment of your receipt of such
paper notices or disclosures. To indicate to us that you are changing your mind, you must
withdraw your consent using the DocuSign ‘Withdraw Consent’ form on the signing page of a
DocuSign envelope instead of signing it. This will indicate to us that you have withdrawn your
consent to receive required notices and disclosures electronically from us and you will no longer
be able to use the DocuSign system to receive required notices and consents electronically from
us or to sign electronically documents from us.

All notices and disclosures will be sent to you electronically

Unless you tell us otherwise in accordance with the procedures described herein, we will provide
electronically to you through the DocuSign system all required notices, disclosures,
authorizations, acknowledgements, and other documents that are required to be provided or
made available to you during the course of our relationship with you. To reduce the chance of
you inadvertently not receiving any notice or disclosure, we prefer to provide all of the required
notices and disclosures to you by the same method and to the same address that you have given
us. Thus, you can receive all the disclosures and notices electronically or in paper format through
the paper mail delivery system. If you do not agree with this process, please let us know as
described below. Please also see the paragraph immediately above that describes the
consequences of your electing not to receive delivery of the notices and disclosures

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  10
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
File ID: 20-3765
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
November 2, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Potable Reuse Exploratory Plan Phase 3 Feasibility Study – Memorandum of Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve a Memorandum of Agreement between the Bay Area Water Supply and Conservation 
Agency, California Water Service Company, City and County of San Francisco Public Utilities Commission, and Silicon Valley 
Clean Water to participate in the Potable Reuse Exploratory Plan Phase 3 Feasibility Study, which will incorporate the City 
of San Mateo as a party to the agreement and commit to a cost share not to exceed $40,000; and authorize the Director of 
Public Works to execute the Memorandum of Agreement in substantially the form attached. 
BACKGROUND:
The San Mateo Clean Water Program is pursuing water reuse options as part of the City of San Mateo's sustainability goals. 
In 2016, a group of water and wastewater utilities in the Bay Area initiated an effort to study potable water reuse 
opportunities in the mid-peninsula region and entered into a Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) to memorialize the 
scope of the study and cost sharing contributions. During the course of the study, the City of San Mateo, through the 
Public Works Department, expressed interest in participating in the study and having the effluent discharge from the new 
wastewater treatment plant considered as a potential source water option. Through its relationship with California Water 
Service Company (CalWater), the City of San Mateo was able to have its future recycled water source included in the 
Potable Reuse Exploratory Plan (PREP) Phase 1 evaluation (Kennedy/Jenks Consultants, December 2017). The objective of 
the PREP Phase 1 Study was to develop a decision tool for the participating agencies, with the goal of performing an initial 
screening of alternatives to provide sufficient information for the PREP parties to determine whether to proceed with 
continued exploration of and investment in a potential regional potable water reuse solution, with a focus on indirect 
potable reuse. 
The PREP Phase 1 Study evaluated groundwater reuse replenishment in the San Mateo Plain Basin and reservoir water 
augmentation at the Crystal Springs Reservoir and Bear Gulch Reservoir. It also evaluated potential water supply options 
from Silicon Valley Clean Water (SVCW) and San Mateo wastewater treatment plants, and alternative locations for 
advanced water purification treatment facilities. The study identified this indirect potable reuse option as conceptually 
feasible and worthy of further consideration and evaluation. 
The participating agencies agreed to continue the process by establishing a Technical Advisory Committee (TAC), including 
participation by City of San Mateo Public Works staff. The TAC team worked collaboratively to develop a recommended 
scope of work for a proposed Phase 2 study to further evaluate costs, challenges, timing, and technical concepts for 
treating and conveying purified water to the Crystal Springs Reservoir. Amendment No. 1 to the 2016 MOU added San 
Mateo to the agreement and established the scope of work for the PREP Phase 2 Concept Study. Finalized in 2019 
(Kennedy/Jenks Consultants, December 2019), the study evaluated options and determined construction costs for an 
advanced treatment water purification facility and pipelines ranging between $310 and $618 million, with annual 
201 of 312

--- page 202 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
operating costs of ranging between $10 and $14 million. This effort also highlighted the need for additional analyses to 
evaluate the impacts of reservoir water augmentation to Crystal Springs Reservoir. Further, the participating agencies 
identified an opportunity to explore direct potable reuse options in addition to the further development on an indirect 
approach. 
The PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study will provide additional analysis issues related to mixing, retention times, and operations 
at the Crystal Springs Reservoir and explore alternatives for direct potable reuse on the San Francisco Mid-Peninsula 
region. The effort will evaluate alternatives, compare costs, benefits, limitations and risks and help determine a path 
forward. Indirect and direct potable water reuse opportunities expand beyond non-potable irrigation. 
While the City of San Mateo is not a water purveyor, the effluent from the wastewater treatment plant could be a valuable 
resource to the region in addressing extended years of drought. Through a regional approach and collaboration with 
partnering agencies, the City would continue to support an integrated water management strategy. Staff recommends 
approval of a Memorandum of Agreement for the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The City of San Mateo’s contribution to the total cost of the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study of $282,161 will be capped at 
$40,000 and will be funded from the operating budget of the Sewer Fund.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
In accordance with Public Resources Code Section 15262, the feasibility study is statutorily exempt from CEQA.
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT AMONG
BAY AREA WATER SUPPLY AND CONSERVATION AGENCY, 
CALIFORNIA WATER SERVICE COMPANY, CITY OF REDWOOD CITY, 
CITY OF SAN MATEO, CITY & COUNTY OF SAN FRANCISCO PUBLIC 
UTILITIES COMMISSION, AND SILICON VALLEY CLEAN WATER 
REGARDING POTABLE REUSE EXPLORATORY PLAN 
PHASE 3 FEASIBILITY STUDY
THIS MEMORANDUM OF AGREEMENT (“Agreement”), made in the State of 
California on this ____ day of _______, 2020, is by and among the Bay Area Water 
Supply and Conservation Agency (“BAWSCA”), California Water Service Company 
(“Cal Water”), City of Redwood City (“Redwood City”), City of San Mateo (“San 
Mateo”), City & County of San Francisco acting by and through its Public Utilities 
Commission (“San Francisco” or “SFPUC”), and Silicon Valley Clean Water, a Joint 
Powers Authority (“SVCW”), referred to collectively herein as the “Parties” and 
individually as a “Party.” 
RECITALS
1. WHEREAS, the Parties represent, own, or operate independent water or wastewater 
treatment systems that collectively serve the needs of over 2.7 million residents and 
businesses in the San Francisco Bay Region; and
2. WHEREAS, the Parties recognize that California is prone to droughts that would be 
exacerbated by climate change; and
3. WHEREAS, the Parties recognize that the use of advanced water purification  
technology for potable reuse is being developed and implemented across the state; 
and 
4. WHEREAS, the Parties recognize that potable reuse may provide water supply 
reliability and/or water quality benefits to the Parties and the public they all serve; 
and 
5. WHEREAS, each Party to this Agreement has a clear objective related to the 
development of a coordinated plan for potable reuse in the San Francisco Bay Region, 
as follows:
Silicon Valley Clean Water and City of San Mateo (Wastewater Agencies): 
To support local, regional, and State goals for recycled water use and promote the 
development of recycled water supplies to provide maximum benefit to our 
service areas.
204 of 312

--- page 205 ---
2
Bay Area Water Supply and Conservation Agency: To identify a potential 
new water supply to meet the dry-year water supply reliability needs of its 
member agencies, as documented in BAWSCA’s Long-Term Reliable Water 
Supply Strategy Phase II Final Report.
California Water Service Company: To identify potential new local water 
supply opportunities and capital projects that will provide supply reliability to our 
Bay Area Peninsula customers. 
City of Redwood City: To identify potential new water supplies, and 
enhance the quality of recycled water to promote beneficial uses. 
San Francisco Public Utilities Commission: To identify potential new 
water supply opportunities to serve existing and new customer demands, 
including the Cities of San Jose and Santa Clara.
6. WHEREAS, the Parties have worked collaboratively since 2016 under a separate 
agreement, dated November 3, 2016, which was subsequently amended in April 2018 
and expired in April 2020, to develop a coordinated plan for potable reuse in the San 
Francisco Bay Region, known as the Potable Reuse Exploratory Plan (“PREP”), 
through the PREP Phase 1 Initial Study and PREP Phase 2 Concept Study; and 
7. WHEREAS, the PREP Phase 1 Initial Study considered potable reuse alternative 
concepts, including reuse through groundwater replenishment and Reservoir Water 
Augmentation (“RWA”) at the SFPUC’s Crystal Spring Reservoir (“CSR”) and Cal 
Water’s Bear Gulch Reservoir; and
8. WHEREAS, the PREP Phase 2 Concept Study further defined the concept of a RWA 
project at CSR and included a parallel study that provided a preliminary evaluation  
of a potable reuse project that augments CSR with purified water; and
9. WHEREAS, the Parties recognize additional study is needed to establish the 
feasibility of the PREP, and SVCW has entered into a contract with a consultant 
(“Consultant”) under which the Consultant will conduct the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility 
Study, as described in the Consultant Scope of Work developed and approved by the 
Parties, which is attached hereto and incorporated herein as Attachment 1; and
10. WHEREAS, SVCW and the Consultant have entered into a separate agreement 
concerning the Consultant Scope of Work and Consultant’s obligations under said 
contract with respect to its performance of the Consultant Scope of Work (“SVCW-
Consultant Agreement”), which is  incorporated herein as part of Attachment 1; and
205 of 312

--- page 206 ---
3
11. WHEREAS, the Parties desire to enter into this Agreement setting forth the 
respective roles and responsibilities of the Parties, and the cost sharing allocations  
and procedures, regarding the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study;  
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of the recitals and mutual obligations of the 
Parties herein expressed, the Parties agree as follows:
1.
DEFINITIONS
The following definitions apply to this Agreement:
a) “Consultant” means the consulting firm Kennedy and Jenks, which has been 
retained by the Contracting Entity to perform the Consultant Scope of Work for 
the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study attached to this Agreement as Attachment 1. 
b) “Contract” means the contract between the Contracting Entity and the Consultant 
under which the Consultant will perform the Consultant Scope of Work for the 
PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, and the SVCW-Consultant Agreement, 
collectively.  
c) “Contracting Entity” means Silicon Valley Clean Water, which has been 
designated by all Parties as the entity to retain the Consultant for the PREP Phase 
3 Feasibility Study and to administer and manage the Contract with the 
Consultant.
d) “Direct Potable Reuse” or “DPR” means tthe delivery of purified water to a 
drinking water plant or a drinking water distribution system without an 
environmental buffer. Additional treatment, monitoring, and/or an engineered 
buffer(s) would be used in place of an environmental buffer to provide equivalent 
protection of public health and response time in the event that the purified water 
does not meet specifications
e) “Indirect Potable Reuse” or “IPR” means the addition of recycled water to 
augment groundwater or surface waters. Groundwater and surface waters are 
considered environmental buffers for providing public health protection benefits, 
such as contaminant attenuation dilution, and time to detect and respond to 
failures before final treatment and distribution. Indirect potable reuse can use 
advanced treated water, but can also be accomplished with tertiary effluent when 
applied by spreading (i.e., groundwater recharge) to take advantage of soil aquifer 
treatment (SAT).
f)
“Party” or “Parties” means BAWSCA, Cal Water, Redwood City, San Mateo, 
SFPUC, and SVCW, either individually or collectively. 
g) “Potable Reuse” means the production of raw water suitable to drinking water 
standards administered by the California Division of Drinking Water through 
206 of 312

--- page 207 ---
4
advanced purification of treated wastewater via Indirect Potable Reuse or Direct 
Potable Reuse.
h) “Potable Reuse Exploratory Plan” or “PREP” means the coordinated plan to 
explore and evaluate Potable Reuse in the San Francisco Bay Region being 
developed by the Parties under this Agreement.
i)
“PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study” means the study that will be prepared through 
this Agreement and the Contract with the Consultant to explore and evaluate the 
feasibility of Direct Potable Reuse or Indirect Potable Reuse for the San Francisco 
Bay Region, as described in the Consultant Scope of Work (Attachment 1).
j)
“SVCW-Consultant Agreement” means the separate agreement between SVCW 
and the Consultant concerning the Consultant Scope of Work and Consultant’s 
obligations under its contract with SVCW with respect to its performance of the 
Consultant Scope of Work, which is attached to the Consultant Scope of Work 
(Attachment 1).  
2.
TERM
a) This Agreement shall become effective on the date that all Parties have signed the 
Agreement, with the condition precedent that SVCW and the Consultant must 
have signed the SVCW-Consultant Agreement for this Agreement to be effective.
b) This Agreement will terminate on December 31, 2022, or when all obligations 
under this Agreement have been performed, whichever occurs first, unless the 
Agreement is earlier terminated as otherwise provided herein.
i.
Payment obligations under Section 8, Cost Sharing and Payment, and 
Section 12, Termination, shall survive the termination of this Agreement 
until obligations under those sections are satisfied.
3.
PURPOSE
The purpose of this Agreement is to:
a) Define the general roles and responsibilities of all Parties, and the additional roles 
and responsibilities of certain Parties, for the development of the PREP Phase 3 
Feasibility Study.  All work associated with the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study is 
to be conducted in accordance with the Agreement, and the Parties agree that no 
work on the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study shall commence until this Agreement 
has been executed by all Parties.
b) Establish the cost sharing allocations among the Parties for the PREP Phase 3 
Feasibility Study and the procedures by which the Parties will contribute their 
individual cost shares and be reimbursed for any funds collected that are not 
expended for the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study.
207 of 312

--- page 208 ---
5
4.
CALIFORNIA ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY ACT
The Parties agree that the work contemplated in this Agreement, as it involves the 
preparation of the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, is exempt from the requirements of 
the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA).
5.
GENERAL ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE PARTIES
The general roles and responsibilities of each of the Parties under this Agreement are as 
follows:
a) Work cooperatively with the other Parties and the Consultant, as applicable, to 
develop the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, as described in the Consultant Scope 
of Work, and complete other related tasks and activities.
b) Commit staff time to work with other Parties and the Consultant, as applicable, to 
develop the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, including but not limited to review 
of deliverables prepared by the Consultant.
c) Commit staff time to work on tasks related to the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study 
that have been identified by the Parties outside the Consultant Scope of Work, 
including such tasks as developing a PREP project fact sheet and identifying 
PREP project benefits to the Parties in order to determine future cost sharing for 
the continued development of the PREP. 
d) Contribute its share of the total actual costs of the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility 
Study, as specified in Section 8 of this Agreement.
e) Share relevant engineering, permitting, regulatory and operational information 
regarding its own facilities and permits with other Parties or the Consultant for the 
benefit of the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, as needed and upon request.
f)
Provide access to facilities and operational data that may be needed for 
developing the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study (such as groundwater 
management, hydrogeology, intakes, aqueducts and pumping plants, transmission 
lines, reservoirs, treatment plants, interties, etc.).  If needed, commit staff time to 
conduct necessary analysis of its own facilities, permits, operational data, 
modeling information, procedures or requirements, or any other data needed for 
the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study and share the information with other Parties 
and/or the Consultant.  Access to facilities will be consistent with, and will 
follow, the facility owner’s standard safety and notification requirements.
g) Provide oversight and review of the Consultant’s deliverables and work product 
for the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study.
208 of 312

--- page 209 ---
6
h) Conduct general work that is needed to advance the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility 
Study’s development. These efforts may include State and Federal grant 
application and grant administration support, website update, and outreach.  
6.
ADDITIONAL ROLES AND RESPONSIBILITIES OF SVCW
The additional roles and responsibilities of SVCW under this Agreement are as follows:
a) Subject to approval by SVCW’s governing board, serve as the Contracting Entity, 
managing and administering the Contract with the Consultant to develop the 
PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, as described in the Consultant Scope of Work 
(Attachment 1) approved by all Parties. 
b) Prepare and transmit to the other Parties invoices for their respective shares of the 
total costs of the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, per Section 8 of this 
Agreement.
c) Receive and pay all invoices from the Consultant for services rendered under the 
Contract to develop the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study.  Costs for the 
Consultant’s services shall be shared among the Parties as described in Section 8 
of this Agreement.  
d) Instruct the Consultant to communicate with all Parties directly about the 
development of the PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study and related activities and 
deliverables.
e) Instruct the Consultant to distribute both draft and final deliverables for the PREP 
Phase 3 Feasibility Study to all Parties directly for review and comment.
f)
Return to the Parties as a reimbursement any funds collected by SVCW under this 
Agreement that are not expended to pay for the Consultant’s services for the 
PREP Phase 3 Feasibility Study, per Section 8 of this Agreement.
g) Ensure that the Consultant abides by the terms of the SVCW-Consultant 
Agreement (Attachment 1).
7.

SFPUC to develop TM #2 describing RWS considerations, assumptions and 
outcomes of the evaluation with summary tables, maps and graphs.  SFPUC to 
provide a Draft and Final TM #2 for inclusion as an appendix to the Phase 3 
Study (Task 3).

role or roles.  If the Contracting Entity is the terminating Party, the obligations of the 
Consultant under the Contract with the Contracting Entity shall also terminate, and it will 
become the responsibilities of the remaining Parties to pursue further development of the

independent of either the Contracting Entity or the Contract entered into by the

CITY OF SAN MATEO

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
November 02, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Basin 4 Collection System Improvements Project – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 4 to the professional design services agreement with Woodard and Curran to provide 
engineering design services for the Basin 4 Collection System Improvements Project in an amount not to exceed $721,439, 
increase the contingency fund by $70,000, and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in 
substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Basin 4 Collection System Improvements Project (Project) is part of the Clean Water Program (CWP) and provides 
important sewer improvements to increase capacity for wet weather flows in the neighborhoods east of Highway 101. 
Engineering design services for the Project were planned to be completed in three phases, with the scope and fee of each 
subsequent phase to be negotiated and executed after the completion of the prior phase: 
Phase 1 - Alternatives Analysis 
Phase 2 - Engineering Design 
Phase 3 - Construction Phase Services 
On July 25, 2017, City Council approved an agreement for engineering design services with Woodard and Curran to 
conduct Phase 1 Alternative Analysis for the Project. Since the original agreement, Amendments 1, 2, and 3 were approved 
to increase the Phase 1 scope and budget. These amendments included increased public outreach support, sanitary sewer 
field testing, hydraulic modeling, coordination between other ongoing CWP projects, additional smoke testing and video 
inspections, and additional pump station analysis. In May 2020, Woodard and Curran completed Phase 1 - Alternatives 
Analysis, which recommended specific packages to improve system capacity and flow management. Upon review of the 
Phase 1 - Alternatives Analysis results, staff recommends one of the packages, Dale/Norton Conveyance Relief package, to 
proceed into Phase 2 – Engineering Design. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The initial approved agreement with Woodard and Curran for the Basin 4 Collection System Improvements Project is in the 
amount of $1,223,000. The prior approved amendments are in the table shown on the following page. Amendment No. 4 
increases the agreement amount by $721,439, bringing the total contract amount to $2,215,258. Amendment No. 4 also 
increases the contingency by $70,000. Funding for Amendment No. 4 is available in the Basin 4 Collection System 
Improvements Project, which has an unencumbered balance of $11.46M and is sufficient to fund this work.

AMENDMENT NO. 4 TO THE AGREEMENT 
BETWEEN THE CITY OF SAN MATEO AND WOODARD & CURRAN, INC. 
FOR PROFESSIONAL DESIGN SERVICES ON THE BASIN 4 COLLECTION 
SYSTEM IMPROVEMENTS 
 
 
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo (“City”), a municipal corporation of the State 
of California, and Woodard & Curran, Inc. (“Consultant”), entered into an Agreement for 
Engineering Services (“Agreement”) on July 25, 2017; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, City and Consultant wish to amend the Agreement to extend the 
term, increase compensation, and add scope. 
 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, the parties agree as follows: 
 
1. 
Section 1 - Scope of Project of the Agreement is amended to reference 
"Exhibit 1” of this Amendment No.4.  Exhibit 1 to the Agreement is 
attached and incorporated by reference.   
 
2. 
Section 8 - Payment of the Agreement is amended to change the fee from 
$1,493,819" to “$2,215,258." 
 
3. 
The remaining terms of the Agreement remain in full force and effect.

SCOPE OF SERVICES 
The Consultant will provide engineering services for all Project Elements listed in this Scope of 
Services. The project, and fee negotiations, will be executed in three phases as listed below. 
Phase 1 (Services completed February 2020) 
• 
Task 1 – General Services 
• 
Task 2 – Alternatives Analysis 
Phase 2  
• 
Task 1 – General Services 
• 
Task 3 – Pre-Design Investigations 
• 
Task 4 – Preliminary (30%) Design 
• 
Task 5 – Final Design 
o Task 5.1 – 60% Design 
o Task 5.2 – 90% Design 
o Task 5.3 – Final (100%) Design and Bid Documents 
• 
Task 6 – Bid Phase Services 
Phase 3 (to be negotiated after Phase 2) 
• 
Task 1 – General Services 
• 
Task 7 – Construction Phase Services 
Tasks that are required of the Consultant under these categories are detailed in the following 
sections. Throughout the design of this project, the Consultant will submit deliverables for review 
and approval by the City and other governing agencies as listed in this scope of services.  
The City reserves the right to discontinue, alter, or postpone services at any time.  The 
Consultant shall not proceed with any changes to the project scope without the City’s approval. 
 
PHASE 2 
TASK 1 – GENERAL SERVICES 
General Services include tasks that will be performed by the Consultant throughout the project. 
These services include:  
• 
Project management 
• 
Risk management 
• 
Workshops and meetings 
• 
Quality control plan 
• 
Management of Subconsultants 
• 
Agency Coordination, Public Outreach Support, and City Meeting Support

Permitting and Environmental Support 
Further information regarding expectations for these services has been provided by the City as a 
separate Clean Water Program (Program) standard in the Draft Design Standards and 
Guidelines. This scope of work is based on the November 2016 version of these standards and

The level of effort for many of the subtasks in Task 1 is related to the duration of the phases. For 
this scope and fee the following durations are assumed: 
• 
Phase 2 total duration is assumed to be 17 months (design started and ended within a 17-
month period) 
Task 1.1 – Project Management 
Task 1.1.1 – General Management 
The Consultant will be responsible for detailed management of the project, including the 
Subconsultants, and will keep the City apprised of the status of the project.  
The Consultant will provide the key management personnel as described in the attached fee 
estimate on this project. The Consultant will not reassign the key project personnel without prior 
approval of the City per the Standard Agreement for Professional Consultant Services. 
Deliverables: 
• 
None. 
Task 1.1.2 – Project Execution Plan (PXP) 
The Consultant will prepare and submit a Project Execution Plan (PXP). The PXP will follow the 
requirements of the Program Design Standards. The PXP that was initially prepared for Phase 1 
will be updated by the Consultant for each subsequent phase. The draft updated PXP for each 
phase will be reviewed for acceptance by the City. The final updated PXP for each phase will 
incorporate all comments from the City. 
Deliverables: 
• 
Draft PXP (Phase 2) (submitted via email). 
• 
Final PXP (Phase 2) incorporating comments from the City (submitted via email). 
Task 1.1.3 – Work Breakdown Structure (WBS) 
The Consultant will prepare and submit a project work breakdown structure (WBS), which 
includes a matrix indicating the budget amounts and man-hours for each task. This includes 
establishing the WBS, defining the Tasks loaded with resources, and defining rules of credits for 
Earned Value by task.  The WBS will be reviewed for acceptance by the City. The approved WBS 
will form the basis for reporting the status of each task in the monthly progress report and project 
invoice. 
Deliverables: 
• 
Project work breakdown structure (submitted via email as part of the monthly progress 
report/invoice)

Task 1.1.4 – Progress Report and Invoices 
The Consultant will prepare and submit monthly progress reports that include a narrative of the 
work completed by task, project decision log, project action/issues item log, upcoming work, 
project issues, budget and schedule status per task, percent complete per task, cost to complete 
per task, potential scope or budget changes, performance indicators, a narrative to explain 
variance from an acceptable performance indicator range, and other important project 
information. 
An Interim Report due on the 25th of each month of the project duration will also be submitted to 
the Program in email format. This report will contain a table detailing the financial status of the 
project current up to the day before the submittal of the interim report. Financial status, including 
total amount spent and amount spent per task, may change in the period between the Interim 
Report and the Progress Report.  
The Consultant will submit the monthly invoices with the monthly progress report and schedule 
as part of the monthly request for payment. 
Deliverables: 
• 
Progress Reports and Invoices (submitted monthly via email) 
• 
Interim Report (submitted monthly on the 25th via email) 
Task 1.1.5 – Project Schedule 
The Consultant will create a level 3 Critical Path Method (CPM) project baseline schedule, 
demonstrating how the Consultant will meet the target date for completion of Phase 2 of the 
project. Consultant shall submit to the City a preliminary schedule within 10 working days after 
Notice to Proceed (NTP). City shall provide comments within 5 working days after receipt of 
preliminary schedule. The Consultant shall incorporate City comments into the preliminary 
schedule and resubmit within 5 working days of receipt of City comments. Once the resubmittal 
is accepted by the City, the schedule will become Phase 2 Baseline Schedule. 
The Consultant shall use Primavera Project Planner (P6) for this purpose.  Consultant will define 
major and/or critical project activities, including a minimum of 15 working days for City, and 20 
working days for regulatory and permitting review. The schedule will expand upon the City’s 
overall project schedule. At a minimum, the schedule will indicate the following: 
• 
Constrained milestone for Project Start date; NTP (this shall be a Start on Constraint) 
• 
Constrained milestone for Project Finish date; contract finish date (this shall be a Finish 
On constraint) 
• 
 
• 
Start and Finish Milestones for project phases; these shall be unconstrained 
• 
Project submittal dates 
• 
Submittal dates for each deliverable 
• 
Meeting and workshop dates 
• 
Verifiable physical percent complete for each activity

All activities shall be appropriately logically linked and have at a minimum of one successor 
and one predecessor, with the exception of the start project milestone and finish

• 
It is acceptable to use either Level of Effort (LOE) activities and/or WBS Summary

The Consultant will maintain the project schedule on a monthly basis. After baseline is set and 
agreed, the Consultant shall prepare a Planned vs. Actual vs. Forecast curve for the Project. 
Curves shall be based on resources loaded schedule. Prior to invoice submittal, the Consultant 
shall evaluate the percent complete for each activity worked on during the billing period. The 
Consultant shall calculate the earned value for the month using approved rules of credits with the 
City. The earned value shall be compared to the planned earn value and the actual invoice value 
for each month. The Consultant shall justify any requests for monies over the planned value and 
explain how the overall budget will be met over the life of the project. 
The Consultant shall use Cost Performance Index (CPI) and Schedule Performance Index (SPI) 
as key indicators and include a monthly justification for any overall project indicator less than 1.00.

Project schedule (submitted monthly via email with the project report)

Project Earned Value, CPI and SPI Analysis (submitted monthly via email with progress 
report) 
• 
Primavera 6 schedule native file (XER file) 
• 
Cost Curves (submitted monthly via email with the project report) 
 
Task 1.1.6 – Logs 
The Consultant will develop and maintain a Decision Log. The log will be used to track project 
decisions and how they were made, for example, design changes or changes in scope. The 
Consultant will submit a copy of the updated Decision Log with each monthly Progress Report. 
The Consultant will develop and maintain an Action/Issues Item Log. The Consultant will submit 
an updated copy of the Action/Issues Item Log at progress meetings and with each monthly 
Progress Report. The log should include the following information: 
• 
Assign an Action Item Number 
• 
Describe the Action Item 
• 
Identify the originator of the Action Item 
• 
Identify the initiation date of the Action Item 
• 
Describe the problem, issue or interest the Action Item is intended to address 
• 
Specify who is responsible for completing the Action Item 
• 
Specify the Action Item due date 
• 
Identify when the Action Item was completed

Task 1.2 – Risk Management 
The Program will take ownership of and maintain the Project Risk Register.  The Project Risk 
Register (PRR) will first be reviewed and revised by the Program PM based on their reassessment 
of risks for Phase 2 of the project. The Consultant will perform a quarterly review of the existing 
risk registers and risk response plan.  The Consultant will provide recommendations if new risks 
are identified and changes to the response plan that need to be updated based on the Project 
status. 
The level of effort for this task assumes there will be no dedicated risk management face-to-face 
meetings and that risk management will be discussed via conference call and/or at the design 
submittal meetings. 
Deliverables: 
• 
Project Risk Register (including quarterly updates). 
• 
Risk Response Plan 
Task 1.3 – Workshops and Meetings 
Task 1.3.1 – Kickoff Meeting  
The Consultant will conduct a kickoff meeting with the City for the design of the Dale/Norton 
project.  At the City’s discretion, this kickoff meeting may be conducted via video conference call.  
Agenda and meeting minutes will be prepared by the Consultant. The kickoff meeting is assumed 
to be two hours long and will be attended by the Project Manager and Pipeline Design Lead, at a 
minimum. 
Task 1.3.2 – Progress Meetings 
The Consultant will conduct monthly project meetings via video conference with the City to review 
the Consultant Project Manager’s report and the status of the project scope, schedule, budget 
and any issues which may affect completion of the project. Meetings should be arranged so that 
the monthly progress report, invoice, and schedule can be submitted the day of each meeting. 
Acceptance of the monthly progress report, invoice, and schedule at this meeting is not 
mandatory; the City has up to five workdays to review and approve the submittal. Agenda and 
meeting minutes will be prepared by the Consultant for project progress meetings.  The Decision 
Log will be updated per discussions conducted in these meetings.  Progress meetings will not be 
conducted during Phase 3 of the project. Bi-weekly construction meetings will replace progress 
meetings in Phase 3. Monthly project progress meetings are assumed to be one hour long.  
Other meetings via conference call will be scheduled on an as-needed basis. The level of effort 
reflects an assumption of bi-weekly “as-needed” meetings for the duration of the project (17

Meeting agendas and minutes for up to 34 meetings.  (Meeting agendas and minutes

Task 1.3.3 –Design Review Workshops 
The Consultant will hold three Design Review workshops. 
Phase 2 Design Review Workshops: The Consultant will conduct three virtual design review 
workshops to update the City of the Consultant’s work progress on the 30%, 60%, and 90% 
Design submittals. Each of the three virtual meetings are assumed to be 2 hours.  These meetings 
shall be by video conference. The purpose of these meetings is to present submittals to the City 
and demonstrate that previous City comments were addressed (as applicable). These meetings 
will also assist the Consultant in keeping the City apprised of the job, reviewing work-in-progress, 
sharing information, discussing project submittals, presenting findings of technical analyses, 
discussing constructability and operation concepts, receiving and resolving comments, and 
obtaining decisions and direction by City staff. 
The City will be able to provide new comments to the Consultant during these workshops. The 
City review period is typically two weeks for each major submittal. At the end of the review period, 
the Consultant will meet with City staff to receive and review City comments. Final adjudication of 
comments will be documented. 
Deliverables: 
• 
Meeting agenda and meeting minutes for three review workshops at the following levels 
of design for each bid package: 
o 30% Design 
o 60% Design 
o 90% Design  
 
Task 1.4 – Quality Control Plan 
The Consultant will update the Quality Assurance/Quality Control (QA/QC) Plan that was 
developed in Phase 1 for implementation of Phase 2. The Consultant’s updated QA/QC Plan will 
be reviewed and approved by the City Project Manager and will include or reference the controls 
necessary for implementation. 
Submittals that contain gross deficiencies or errors requiring a significant amount of the City staff 
time for checking will be returned without review until the City is satisfied that a thorough 
Consultant’s review, checking and correction for coherence, consistency, spelling, etc., has been 
performed. 
Level of effort for quality control reviews and related activities are included under other tasks.

Task 1.6 – Permitting and Environmental Support 
Task 1.6.1 – Permitting  
In Phase 2, for applicable Project Elements of this Scope of Work, the Consultant will provide 
contract documents which ensure that facility features and performance and construction 
procedures comply with conditions of existing permits and permits required to construct this 
project. Construction drawings, specifications, and supplemental drawings will be prepared, as 
necessary in the format required to obtain permits necessary for construction for this project. 
The Consultant shall obtain local/county, state/regional, and federal permits listed below that are 
required for the bid package, including but not limited to environmental permits and encroachment 
permits, as listed below. The Consultant will complete permit applications, prepare supporting 
documentation for the permit applications as required by the issuing agency, and furnish the 
required number of copies of construction drawings and exhibits. Attendance at meetings is not 
included as part of this task. The Consultant will ensure permit applications are submitted in a 
timely fashion. 
Permit fees will be paid directly by the City and will not be deemed part of Consultant’s fee. 
Two permits are assumed for the Dale/Norton Conveyance Relief Project. The permits to be 
obtained during design of the Dale/Norton Conveyance Relief Project include: 
• 
San Mateo County – Subsurface Drilling Permit and Geotechnical Drilling Permit (to be 
obtained by Woodard & Curran’s geotechnical subconsultant) 
• 
California Occupational Safety and Health – Underground Classification (for trenchless 
pipe installation) 
Deliverables: 
• 
Permit applications for: 
o San Mateo County – Subsurface Drilling Permit and Geotechnical Drilling Permit 
o California Occupational Safety and Health – Underground Classification

new significant impacts or result in a substantial increase in the severity of impacts that were 
already identified in the Programmatic EIR. It is thus assumed that supplemental CEQA review

PHASE 2 – CONSTRUCTION BID PACKAGE ASSUMPTIONS  
Phase 2 focuses on design and bid support services. In order to prepare a scope of work and fee 
estimate, it is necessary to describe the improvements that are assumed to be designed and 
constructed. The following is a description of the assumed project. Changes in these assumptions 
may necessitate an amendment to be discussed with the City and Program.  The bid package is 
shown on the figure on the following page. 
Dale/Norton Conveyance Relief Project. This bid package includes: 
• 
Approximately 630-feet of 12-inch gravity sewer to be installed with trenchless methods 
along Anna Street, Dale Avenue, and South Norfolk Street. 
• 
Approximately 1,660-feet of 15-inch gravity sewer to be installed with trenchless methods 
along Kehoe Avenue, South Norfolk Street, Hemlock Avenue, and Patricia Avenue. 
• 
Connection to the existing sewer system in several locations, including the influent pipeline 
to the Dale Avenue Pump Station.

Task 3.1 – Survey 
Consultant’s surveying subconsultant will conduct field surveys as required. Topographic 
information used on the construction plans will be generated from a field survey. The City will not 
provide the aerial survey information to Consultant for use on the project. There are four subtasks 
associated with Task 3.1: 1) Project Control, 2) Boundary Survey for the determination of the 
street rights-of-way, 3) Topographic Survey, and 4) geotechnical boring and pothole survey 
(assumed to be completed together in one mobilization). 
The project control will be carried out using GPS, conventional and electronic leveling techniques. 
Consultant will set up a GPS control network to the anticipated control points, extend that control 
to the project areas with conventional traverse techniques, and run levels to the main control 
points. Horizontal datum will be the most current published NAD83 coordinates and the vertical 
datum will be City of San Mateo datum plus 100 feet.  The City of San Mateo vertical datum 
conversion chart is Appendix A1 of SMCWP_CSD14_Survey_and_Mapping_Final.pdf. 
The boundary surveys will be based on found street monuments and filed map information. 
Individual parcel lines will not be determined and owner information for parcels along the routes 
will not be mapped. Individual lot lines may be shown graphically for viewing purposes only. 
The mapping will show spot elevations, contour lines, and planimetric data along the project 
routes with mapping limits being at least back-of-walk to back-of-walk. The survey control and 
basis of bearings/benchmark statements will be shown on the overall topographic mapping and 
the map will be signed by the licensed land surveyor in charge.  
Survey field crews will locate utilities within the limits of back-of-walk to back-of-walk for the 
pipeline alignments. Consultant will obtain measured invert information for the sanitary sewer 
manholes, storm drain manholes, and storm drain drop inlets/catch basins as well as manholes 
that branch off of the main line as needed. This information will be added to the overall mapping 
as manhole/drop inlet details.  
Once the geotechnical borings and utility potholes have been completed, subconsultant will also 
add the horizontal and vertical position of the boring and pothole locations to the mapping.  
The Consultant will be responsible for obtaining permits to perform the survey and providing 
necessary traffic control. A detailed description of the survey requirements and documentation is 
provided in the Program’s Draft Design Standards and Guidelines. The survey will be completed 
before Consultant proceeds to Task 4.  
Deliverables: 
• 
Electronic survey files for use in developing project plans, in AutoCAD format. 
Assumptions: 
• 
The new sewer alignments identified in Phase 1 connect to existing sewers in streets.  
Currently there is no need to survey the location or the invert elevations of existing 
backyard manholes.  If it becomes necessary to survey backyard manholes, the City shall 
provide support with outreach efforts by notifying and coordinating with property owners 
and tenants to provide access.  It is assumed that City escorts for survey crews will not 
be required. If the manholes are buried under landscaping or otherwise inaccessible, the 
City will be responsible for uncovering the manholes and making them accessible.

Task 3.2 – Utility Coordination 
The Consultant will provide utility coordination services, including notifications to providers along 
the project corridors. Utility coordination will be provided at 30%, 60%, and 90% design phases, 
after the submittal of each design phase deliverable. Utility coordination services include: 
• 
Prepare and send written project notifications to identified utility owners, including copies 
of the design plans. 
• 
Provide written requests for existing utility mapping from utility owners identified by 
Underground Service Alert (U.S.A.) within the area of the project. 
• 
Using information gathered during subsurface utility investigations (Task 3.3), identify 
utility conflicts, and share and confirm lists with utility owners via email and/or telephone. 
• 
Evaluate relocation alternatives with the utility owners and project team via email and/or 
telephone. 
This Task does not include any face-to-face meetings with utility owners. Level of effort is as 
defined in the fee estimate.  
Deliverables: 
• 
Copies of notifications and correspondence with utility owners. 
Task 3.3 – Subsurface Utility Engineering Investigation (Potholing) 
The Consultant will perform a potholing investigation for existing underground utilities within the 
project limits and incorporate the resulting utility information onto the 60% design level drawings.  
The Consultant’s potholing subconsultant will perform up to 15 utility potholes using air-vacuum 
excavation to verify the horizontal and vertical location of underground utilities along the project 
alignments within the City of San Mateo. Consultant will prepare a potholing plan, showing the 
location of proposed utility potholes after initial correspondence with utility owners (Task 3.2) has 
been completed. Once the requested utility has been exposed, pertinent utility data will be collected 
that will include the utility type, material composition, general soil characteristics, depth from 
surface to top of utility, estimated diameter or size, and a photo of the exposed utility. After the 
collection of utility data has been completed, the pothole will be restored to its previous condition 
using 
native backfill material and the appropriate surface restoration materials per the 
requirements set forth by the City of San Mateo. Potholes will be marked in the field with MAG 
nail in asphalt, chiseled X in concrete or wooden lath in natural ground and pertinent utility data 
will be recorded on the ground surface with white paint displaying the pothole number, utility 
size, type, and depth. The results of the field work will be presented in an electronic (PDF) report 
that will include: pertinent utility data, longitudinal and latitudinal coordinates, and photos. 
Deliverables: 
• 
Electronic (PDF) report including pertinent utility data as outlined above, longitudinal and 
latitudinal coordinates, and photos. 
Assumptions: 
• 
No encroachment permit from the City of San Mateo is required to perform the 
potholing services.  The potholing subconsultant will prepare a traffic control plan for

Task 3.4 – Geotechnical Investigation  
Task 3.4.1 
Research 
The Consultant’s geotechnical subconsultant will research geotechnical-related data for the 
project area from: 
• 
McMillen Jacobs Associates archives 
• 
City of San Mateo archives (as provided by the City) 
• 
Historic aerial photographs and topographic maps 
• 
U.S. Geological Survey and California Geologic Survey maps 
• 
U.S. Soil/Natural Resources Conservation Service maps 
• 
Association of Bay Area Governments maps. 
 
Findings will be provided in the geotechnical report.  
Task 3.4.2 
Test Boring, CPT and Groundwater-Level Monitoring Plan 
Consultant will review preliminary planned project and propose up to four locations for 
geotechnical test borings. At each location, a test boring in native ground to ≤25 feet (the test 
boring depth extends a minimum of 5 feet below the proposed sewer pipeline invert) will be 
performed.  One of these four borings will be completed as a geotechnical groundwater level 
monitoring well with a data logger.  One day of Cone Penetration Tests (up to six CPTs up to 50-feet 
below ground surface) will be performed.  
Deliverables: 
• 
Map of proposed and revised proposed test borings, CPTs, and well locations.

Task 3.4.3 
Test Boring, CPT and Groundwater-Level Monitoring Well Permits and 
License 
A license from the City of San Mateo will be obtained for the geotechnical investigation, including 
for the drilling contractor. This task assumes that there will be no encroachment permit and no 
inspection fees from the City. 
 
Permits from San Mateo County for drilling test borings, pushing CPTs, and installing the 
groundwater level monitoring well will be obtained.  
 
A contingent assumption is that the project specifications will make abandonment of the wells the 
responsibility of the contractor(s) that will be awarded the contract to construct the projects, that 
the contractor(s) will acquire related well-abandonment permits from the County, and that the 
abandonments will be performed in accordance with County requirements.  The County does not 
allow environmental sampling and testing from permitted geotechnical borings, CPTs, and 
groundwater-level monitoring wells. 
 
Deliverables: 
• 
City of San Mateo licenses 
• 
San Mateo County permit 
Task 3.4.4 
USA Field Marking and Notification for Geotechnical Investigation 
Consultant will field mark and notify Underground Service Alert (USA) of approved test boring, 
CPT, and groundwater-level monitoring well locations prior to drilling. Consultant shall obtain 
necessary permissions from utility owners for completing the geotechnical field work adjacent or 
in close proximity to existing infrastructure. Consultant is not responsible for damage to 
underground utilities not clearly identified nor properly marked in accordance with the USA 
requirements by the time test borings are drilled. 
 
Deliverable:  
• 
USA notification receipts, on request. 
Task 3.4.5 
Traffic Control for Geotechnical Investigation 
Consultant will prepare and submit a traffic control plan to be in place during the drilling of test 
borings, pushing CPTs, and installation of the groundwater-level monitoring wells. This scope of 
work assumes that the plan can consist of photocopies from the Manual on Uniform Traffic 
Control Plans, and that the plan will not require flagmen. 
 
Deliverable:  
• 
Traffic control plan, submitted to the City of San Mateo. 
 
Consultant will provide limited traffic control during the drilling of test borings, pushing CPTs, and 
installation of groundwater-level monitoring wells in accordance with the traffic control plan (i.e., 
static cones and signage). This proposal allows for no more than two days of traffic control 
provided by a professional traffic control company (no flagmen). Any additional traffic control 
requirements from the City are not within the scope of services and the budget.

Page 14 of 24 
Task 3.4.6 
Test Borings, Groundwater Level Monitoring Wells, and Cone Penetration 
Tests 
Test Borings: At each of the four locations described in Task 3.4.2, Consultant will drill a test 
boring in native ground to a depth of ≤25 feet to characterize in-situ native ground conditions 
(groundwater depth, and soil types and consistency). The proposed depth is such that each boring 
will be to a minimum of 5 feet below the invert of the planned sewer pipeline.  One boring will be 
completed as a groundwater level monitoring well with a data logger. 
 
A continuous log of the ground conditions encountered in the test borings will be maintained. 
Disturbed and “undisturbed” ground samples will be taken at 5-foot average intervals.  
 
Consultant will complete one day of field investigations using Cone Penetration Tests (CPT) up to 
a maximum of 50-feet to identify the vertical location of the soil interface at critical locations in the 
project area.  The exact number of CPTs completed will depend on the location, depth and time 
to advance each, but is estimated that up to six CPTs up to a maximum depth of 50-feet below 
ground surface may be completed in one day. 
 
Test borings and CPTs will be backfilled with cement grout and asphalt patching to match existing 
pavement elevations where applicable. 
 
This scope of work and budget is based on the following allowances: 
 
 
Test borings and CPTs are accessible and drillable in City streets. 
 
Borings and CPTs will be permitted between the hours of 8 AM and 5 PM. 
 
All four test borings to ≤25 feet can be completed in a total of one 12-hour work day.  
This includes mobilization and demobilization to and from the project site; the driller 
will only complete work in City right-of-way during the permitted hours of 8AM to 5PM.  
 
No subsurface obstructions and no concrete pavements requiring coring are 
encountered. 
 
Pavement restoration will be with cold-patch asphalt. 
 
USA marking removal is not required. 
 
Well abandonment will be included as part of the pipeline construction contracts by the 
contractor(s) and are not included in this scope of work. 
 
Deliverable: 
• 
Draft boring logs. 
• 
Draft CPT logs. 
Task 3.4.7 
 Disposal of Drilled Cuttings from Test Borings 
Consultant will off-haul and dispose of drilled cuttings from the test borings. The proposal is 
contingent on the cuttings being nonhazardous and disposable without restrictions. If potentially 
hazardous materials are identified visually or by odor within exploratory borings, Consultant will 
notify the City as soon as possible of such occurrence. Consultant will terminate the field 
exploration unless the City provides written authorization to proceed. Costs incurred as a result of 
encountering suspected hazardous materials will be charged on a time-and-expense basis, which 
may be over and above the estimated fee for the exploration. An allowance of $10,000 for disposal

TASK 4 – PRELIMINARY (30%) DESIGN 
Projects selected during the Alternatives Analysis phase will be used as the basis for Preliminary 
(30%) Design. The intent is for all significant project design decisions to be made before the start 
of Task 5 - Final Design. At the end of Preliminary Design, major design elements should be 
established and major structural elements and pipeline alignments should be well defined. The 
extent of the design and the number and type of drawings should also be established.

Preliminary Design includes the following main elements: Preliminary Design services (Task 4)

Task 4.1 – Preliminary Design Technical Memorandum (TM)  
A Preliminary Design Technical Memoranda will be produced for the Dale/Norton Conveyance 
Relief Project.  The Dale/Norton Conveyance Relief TM will document the preliminary design of 
the proposed facilities and accompany a separate package that includes drawings associated 
with the TM. The draft TM will be prepared and submitted to the City for review and subsequently 
discussed in detail at a review workshop (Task 1.3.3). The Consultant will respond to one set of 
consolidated City review comments in writing and incorporate comments into the Final TM as 
applicable. City comments on the Draft TM will be incorporated into a Final TM for submission to 
the City. 
The TMs shall include the following: 
1. Executive Summary 
2. Introduction and Background 
3. Collection System Hydraulics 
• 
Update hydraulic analysis for diversion and relief lines prepared in the Alternatives 
Analysis (Phase 1, Task 2). Updates may include refinements in pipeline alignments 
based on preliminary design, results of sensitivity analyses to assumptions on design 
wet weather events or low flow conditions, and analysis of bypass pumping 
alternatives. The Modeling TM, as specified in Section 5.2 of Collection System Draft 
Design Guideline CSDG10, Hydraulic Modeling Coordination (March 2016), will be 
prepared as part of this Task and added as an appendix to the Preliminary Design TM. 
4. Pipeline Improvements 
• 
Finalize pipe sizes. 
• 
Finalize horizontal alignment and determine preliminary vertical alignment for 
diversion piping. 
• 
Identify new pipe material alternatives. 
• 
Finalize pipe installation method. 
• 
Identify trenchless technology for new installation locations and requirements. 
• 
Determine installation requirements for special areas (flood plain, hazardous materials 
areas, etc.) based on desktop studies. 
• 
Locate existing and new manholes and/or junction structures. 
• 
Determine utility relocations and/or demolitions required. 
• 
Determine traffic control required. 
• 
Prepare preliminary pipe design calculations. 
• 
Determine bypass pumping requirements for existing system.

TASK 5 – FINAL DESIGN 
Final Design includes two main elements: Final Design (Task 5) and elements of General 
Services (Task 1). General descriptions of the tasks and deliverables for each of the main 
elements are provided in the following sections. Further information regarding expectations for 
design deliverables have been issued as separate program standards in the Draft Design 
Standards and Guidelines  
The Consultant will provide engineering services to prepare biddable plans and technical 
specifications based on the design concepts and criteria developed during Preliminary Design. 
The City will be responsible for preparation of Front End Specifications. The Final Design will be 
documented in three review phases (60%, 90%, and 100% design). The design packages will be 
submitted to the City for general review at the end of each phase. Sets sealed by a California 
licensed engineer will be submitted for the final bid documents. Formal workshops will be 
conducted to review the 60% and 90% design packages with the City. The City review period will 
be two weeks for each deliverable. Focused bi-weekly conference calls will also be held 
throughout the Final Design to solicit input from City staff as outlined in Task 1.3.2. The Consultant 
will prepare the Final Bid Documents incorporating comments from the City’s reviews. 
The Consultant will maintain an up-to-date comments log in electronic format on City comments 
received as a result of each submittal review. City comments will be incorporated into the next 
submittal, as appropriate.  For each submittal, the City will provide one set of consolidated 
comments. 
The Consultant will assist the City in providing clarification and responses to plan check 
comments as needed for questions that may arise during the planning and permit application 
processes.

The 60% Dale/Norton Conveyance Relief Design submittal will include: 
• 
Drawings in progress

o Standard Details (Civil, Structural, etc.) as needed – The Program will be 
providing standard details for review and edit by the Consultant. Consultant shall 
also add additional details not provided and as necessary for construction.  
• 
Draft technical specifications

Task 5.2 – 90% Design Submittal   
For the 90% Design Submittal, the major design elements are well-established and 
supplementary/auxiliary design elements are in progress between the 60% and 90% Design 
Submittal. Drawings for all disciplines will be substantially complete. The submittal will include 
existing utilities adjacent to or within the construction area, drawing index, legend, etc. 
Specifications will be substantially complete. 
This submittal will include finished, checked and complete plans and specifications. No new 
drawings and/or specification sections by the Consultant will be expected after this stage. City 
comments on the previous submittal will have been resolved, rejected, addressed, and/or 
incorporated in this submittal. The project is essentially finished and submitted as 100% complete. 
The only missing effort is the City final review and regulatory agency approval with comment 
incorporation. 
Consultant’s checking will include a review of deliverables within each discipline (i.e., drawings, 
detailed specifications, project support documentation, etc.) and an inter-discipline coordination 
cross-check to correct discrepancies among the project documents. 
Discipline calculations, databases, construction cost estimates, schedule, and other project 
support documentation will be updated to reflect the status of the Drawings and Detailed 
Specifications and will support the 90% Design Submittal workshop. 
An updated construction cost estimate (AACE Class 2) and construction sequencing plan and 
schedule will be included with the deliverables. 
Task 5.3 – Final (100%) Design and Bid Documents 
Following receipt of City and regulatory agency review comments on the 90% Design Submittal, 
the Consultant will prepare the Final (100%) Design and submit the Final Bid Documents.  
The Final Bid Documents will include finished, checked, and completed plans and specifications 
and will incorporate City comments from previous submittals, workshops, and constructability 
reviews as appropriate. Prior to submittal, the Consultant will have performed an inter-discipline 
cross-check of the design changes made since 90% design and corrected the related 
discrepancies. The Consultant will not add any new drawings or make any changes to the plans 
or specifications that are not a result of comments received by the City, regulatory review, or a 
final in-house quality control check. The Consultant will document in-house changes and submit 
them to the City along with the Final Bid Documents. 
The Final Design submittal will also include final databases, reports, control strategies, 
construction schedules, cost estimates, and project documentation. 
The process of assisting the City in obtaining the required permits will be completed.

carefully and thoroughly, and if you can access this information electronically to your
satisfaction and agree to these terms and conditions, please confirm your agreement by clicking
the ‘I agree’ button at the bottom of this document. 
Getting paper copies
At any time, you may request from us a paper copy of any record provided or made available
electronically to you by us. You will have the ability to download and print documents we send
to you through the DocuSign system during and immediately after signing session and, if you
elect to create a DocuSign signer account, you may access them for a limited period of time
(usually 30 days) after such documents are first sent to you. After such time, if you wish for us to
send you paper copies of any such documents from our office to you, you will be charged a

procedure described below.

change your mind and tell us that thereafter you want to receive required notices and disclosures
only in paper format. How you must inform us of your decision to receive future notices and
disclosure in paper format and withdraw your consent to receive notices and disclosures
electronically is described below. 
Consequences of changing your mind
If you elect to receive required notices and disclosures only in paper format, it will slow the
speed at which we can complete certain steps in transactions with you and delivering services to
you because we will need first to send the required notices or disclosures to you in paper format,
and then wait until we receive back from you your acknowledgment of your receipt of such
paper notices or disclosures. To indicate to us that you are changing your mind, you must
withdraw your consent using the DocuSign ‘Withdraw Consent’ form on the signing page of a
DocuSign envelope instead of signing it. This will indicate to us that you have withdrawn your
consent to receive required notices and disclosures electronically from us and you will no longer
be able to use the DocuSign system to receive required notices and consents electronically from
us or to sign electronically documents from us.

authorizations, acknowledgements, and other documents that are required to be provided or
